The First Interpretation: Worship Is for the Believers
Baqillani gives the first interpretation of Quran 51:56 by restricting it to believers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's first interpretation of Quran 51:56, which restricts the purpose of creation to those whom Allah knows will worship Him.

Core Idea
Allah created some for worship and some for Hell—both by His knowledge.

Imam Baqillani tackles a common objection: if Allah created all for worship, why do many not worship? His first response is that the verse refers only to those whom Allah knows will worship, as another verse confirms He created many for Hell. This lesson introduces that interpretation and its supporting evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and Baqillani's response
Read the Arabic passage from the objection through the first interpretation, including the citation of the verse about Hell.
Notice how Baqillani uses another Quranic verse to support his interpretation.
2
Identify the key move
Baqillani says 'He intended some of the jinn and humans'. This restricts the general statement. Understand why this is necessary to avoid implying that all are created for worship despite clear reality.
3
Reflect on divine knowledge and creation
Consider how this interpretation reconciles Allah's statement with the fact that many disbelieve. It does not deny creation of disbelievers but assigns a different purpose to them.
The supporting verse about Hell shows that creation includes both believers and disbelievers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
فإن قالوا : فما معنى قوله تعالى وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون ؟
قيل لهم : أراد بعض الجن والإنس، وهم الذين علم أنهم يعبدونه . لأنه قال تعالى في آية أخرى: ﴿ ولقد ذرأنا لجهنم كثيراً من الجن والإنس ﴾ أي : إنه خلق لجهنم كثيراً من الجن والإنس .
فإن قالوا : معنى ذلك : «إنَّا سنذراً».
قيل لهم : وقوله : إلا ليطاع بإذن الله يعني : في الآخرة ؛ وقوله ليعبدون يعني : في المعاد وإن عبـادتـه والاعتراف بـه والتصديق له يقع في الآخرة اضطراراً، وإن كان من جنس الطاعة إذا وقع اختياراً. ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون المراد بقوله : وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون أي : ما خلقتهم إلا لأمرهم بعبادتي . ويكون المقصود بالأمر بالعبادة من بلغ حد التكليف من عقلاء الجنّ والإنس دون غيرهم فسمّى الأمر بالعبادة عبادة لما بينهما من التعلق. وهذا أيضاً ليس ببعيد في التأويل.
A question: If they say: What is the meaning of His statement, Most High: 'And I did not create the jinn and humans except to worship Me'? It is said to them: He intended some of the jinn and humans, those whom He knows will worship Him. Because He said, Most High, in another verse: 'And We have certainly created for Hell many of the jinn and humans' — meaning He created for Hell many of the jinn and humans. If they say: The meaning of that is 'We will abandon them'. It is said to them: His statement 'Except to be obeyed by permission of Allah' means in the Hereafter; and His statement 'to worship Me' means in the final return, and worship of Him, acknowledgment of Him, and affirmation of Him will occur in the Hereafter out of necessity, even if it is of the type of obedience that occurs voluntarily. It is also possible that the intended meaning of His statement 'And I did not create the jinn and humans except to worship Me' is: I did not create them except to command them to worship Me. And the intended meaning of the command to worship applies to those who have reached the level of moral obligation among the rational jinn and humans, excluding others. So the command to worship is called worship due to the connection between them. And this is not far-fetched in interpretation.
Source pages p. 360

Commentary
This passage addresses another objection about a verse that seems to indicate all jinn and humans were created to worship God, yet many do not worship. Baqillani provides two interpretations. The first interpretation restricts the creation for worship to those whom God knows will worship, citing another verse about creating many for Hell. This shows that God creates both believers and disbelievers, each for their destined end. The objector then raises a further objection using the phrase 'We will abandon them', implying God leaves them without guidance. The answer explains that obedience 'by permission of Allah' refers to the Hereafter, where all will obey out of compulsion, and worship in the afterlife is an acknowledgment that occurs necessarily, not voluntarily. This means the verse about worship in this life is not about the compulsion of the afterlife. The second interpretation says the verse means God created them to command them to worship, i.e., to make worship obligatory. This command applies only to those who are morally accountable, not to all beings. This is a reasonable interpretation.

Key Terms
العبادة
الجن
الإنس

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse 'I created jinn and humans only to worship Me' implies that every individual jinn and human is created for the purpose of worship and will inevitably worship.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the verse refers only to those whom Allah knows will worship, not all of creation, as evidenced by another verse stating He created many for Hell.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani's first interpretation, who are the 'jinn and humans' created for worship?
A) All jinn and humans
B) Only the believers among them
C) Only the disbelievers
D) Only the prophets

Key Takeaway
Baqillani interprets Quran 51:56 as referring to those whom Allah knows will worship, not all of creation.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If Allah created some jinn and humans for Hell based solely on His knowledge, where does that leave your own personal responsibility? Are you truly striving in worship, or are you presuming upon His knowledge that you are among the believers?
?
Reading this lesson, you learned that Quran 51:56 does not guarantee every person is created to worship. What if you are one of those 'created for Hell'? How does that possibility change the urgency with which you turn to Allah today?
?
Baqillani’s interpretation separates divine knowledge from command. Do you live as though your actions are predetermined, or do you feel the weight of your choices knowing that Allah already knows their outcome? How will you reconcile this with your next decision to obey or disobey?

Sub-Objection and Second Interpretation: Command to Worship and the Hereafter
Baqillani addresses a sub-objection and offers a second interpretation of the verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's response to the sub-objection about 'سنذراً' and his second interpretation that the verse refers to the command to worship.

Core Idea
The verse can mean command to worship, and ultimate obedience occurs in the Hereafter.

After the first interpretation, the objector raises another point: the phrase 'We will abandon them' (سنذراً) might imply God leaves people without guidance. Baqillani counters that the verse about obedience 'by permission of Allah' refers to the Hereafter, where worship is compelled. He then offers a second interpretation: the verse means God created them to command them to worship.

Guided Path
1
Read the sub-objection and response
Read the Arabic from 'فإن قالوا : معنى ذلك : «إنَّا سنذراً»' through the end of the passage.
Note the two parts: first the response about the Hereafter, then the second interpretation.
2
Understand the Hereafter interpretation
Baqillani says 'except to be obeyed by permission of Allah' means in the Hereafter, where worship is forced. This addresses the objection by shifting the timeframe.
This shows that the verse about worship in this life is not contradicted by the afterlife compulsion.
3
Grasp the second interpretation
The second interpretation says 'to worship Me' means 'to command them to worship Me'. This eases the difficulty because command does not imply actual worship.
Baqillani finds this plausible.

Interpreting 'As for Thamud, We Guided Them, But They Preferred Blindness'
Baqillani explains Quran 41:17 about why Thamud chose error after guidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's two interpretations of Quran 41:17 and how they reconcile divine guidance with human free will.

Core Idea
God's guidance is effective, but humans choose their response.

This passage addresses a common question about a Quranic verse that seems to suggest God's guidance can be rejected. Baqillani offers two plausible interpretations that preserve both divine guidance and human responsibility. As you read, pay attention to how he uses evidence from another verse to support the second interpretation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the literal translation. Let the structure of the question and answer come through.
2
Identify the two interpretations
The passage presents two possible meanings for the verse. Find each one and notice how they differ in who is being guided and who is choosing blindness.
3
Understand the supporting evidence
Notice that the second interpretation is supported by another Quranic verse that states Thamud were two quarreling parties. Consider how this strengthens the interpretation.
The supporting verse is from Surah An-Naml (27:45) or Al-A'raf (7:73)? Actually it's 27:45.
4
Reflect on the theological balance
Think about how these interpretations resolve the apparent tension between God's guidance and human rejection. Baqillani shows that guidance is offered but individuals or groups may reject it.
This connects to broader discussions about qadar (predestination) in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
وإن سألوا فقالوا : ما معنى قوله : وأما ثمود فهديناهم فاستحبوا العمى على الهدى ؟ .
قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أن قوماً من أصحاب ثمود آمنوا فاهتدوا، ثم ارتدوا عن الإيمان وكفروا واستحبّوا العمى على الهدى. ويمكن أن يكون أراد أنه هدى فريقاً من ثمود فاستحب فريق آخر العمى على الهدى . لأن الله تعالى أخبر أنهم فريقان فقال عزّ من قائل : ولقد أرسلنا إلى ثمود أخاهم صالحاً أن اعبدوا الله فإذا هم فريقان يختصمون.
A question: If they ask and say: What is the meaning of His statement: 'As for Thamud, We guided them, but they preferred blindness over guidance'? It is said to them: The meaning of that is that a group of the people of Thamud believed and were guided, then they apostatized from faith and disbelieved and preferred blindness over guidance. And it is possible that He intended that He guided a party of Thamud, and another party preferred blindness over guidance. Because God, Most High, informed that they were two parties, so He said, Mighty and Majestic: 'And We sent to Thamud their brother Salih, [saying], Worship God, and at once they were two parties quarreling.'
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage deals with a question about the verse 'As for Thamud, We guided them, but they preferred blindness over guidance' (Quran 41:17). The objection likely concerns how God can guide a people and yet they choose error. Baqillani gives two possible interpretations. The first interpretation says that the guidance was effective for some (they believed), but then those same people apostatized and chose disbelief. So the verse refers to those who were initially guided but later rejected. The second interpretation says that God guided one party (the believers) while another party (the disbelievers) preferred blindness. The latter is supported by another verse that states Thamud were divided into two quarreling factions. This explanation reconciles divine guidance with human choice: guidance is offered to all, but different groups respond differently.

Key Terms
الهدى
العمى
الارتداد
الفريقان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The verse implies that God's guidance is ineffective or that God guides some to disbelief.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that guidance is effective for those who accept it; the verse either refers to apostates who rejected after guidance, or to two distinct groups—one guided and one wilfully blind.

Checkpoint

A) All Thamud were guided by God
B) Only one party was guided, another preferred blindness
C) None of Thamud were guided
D) God forced them to choose blindness

Key Takeaway
Baqillani reconciles divine guidance and human choice by showing that the verse refers to initial guidance followed by apostasy or to two distinct groups.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Two Interpretations of 'Created to Worship'
Baqillani interprets the verse about jinn and humans created for worship.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two valid interpretations of the verse about creation for worship, showing how Islamic theology accommodates nuanced understandings of divine commands.

Core Idea
Divine worship can mean the command to worship or the eschatological acknowledgment.

Imam Baqillani provides two plausible interpretations of the famous verse "I created jinn and mankind only to worship Me." Rather than limiting to a single literal meaning, he shows that the verse can refer to the inevitable worship in the Hereafter or to the divine command itself. This flexibility demonstrates the depth of Quranic exegesis.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the two distinct interpretations Baqillani presents.
Focus on the terms اضطرار and اختيار.
2
Identify key terms
Look at the terms اضطرار (necessity), اختيار (choice), تكليف (legal responsibility), and تأويل (interpretation). Understand their roles.
These terms are central to the two interpretations.
3
Understand the first interpretation
The first interpretation holds that 'worship' refers to the inevitable acknowledgment of Allah in the Hereafter, which is necessary, though it resembles voluntary obedience in this world.
This interpretation emphasizes that ultimate submission to Allah is unavoidable.
4
Understand the second interpretation
The second interpretation says the verse means Allah created them only to command them to worship. The command itself is called 'worship' because of its connection to the act.
This interpretation focuses on the divine command as the purpose of creation.
5
Reflect on validity
Consider why Baqillani considers both interpretations valid and not far-fetched. This shows the breadth of theological reasoning.
The diversity of interpretation is a strength in Islamic thought.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قيل لهم : وقوله : إلا ليطاع بإذن الله يعني : في الآخرة ؛ وقوله : ليعبدون يعني : في المعاد وإن عبادته والاعتراف به والتصديق له يقع في الآخرة اضطراراً، وإن كان من جنس الطاعة إذا وقع اختياراً. ويمكن أيضاً أن يكون المراد بقوله : وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون أي : ما خلقتهم إلا لأمرهم بعبادتي . ويكون المقصود بالأمر بالعبادة من بلغ حد التكليف من عقلاء الجنّ والإنس دون غيرهم فسمّى الأمر بالعبادة عبادة لما بينهما من التعلق. وهذا أيضاً ليس ببعيد في التأويل.
It was said to them: And His saying: 'except to be obeyed by the permission of Allah' means: in the Hereafter; and His saying: 'to worship Me' means: at the resurrection, although His worship and acknowledgment of Him and affirmation of Him occur in the Hereafter necessarily, even if it is of the kind of obedience when it occurs voluntarily. It is also possible that the intended meaning of His saying: 'And I did not create the jinn and mankind except to worship Me' is: I did not create them except to command them to worship Me. And the intended meaning by the command to worship is those who have reached the level of legal responsibility from among the rational ones of jinn and mankind, not others. So He called the command to worship 'worship' because of the connection between them. And this also is not far-fetched in interpretation.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage offers two interpretations of the Quranic verse 'وما خلقت الجن والإنس إلا ليعبدون' (I created the jinn and mankind only to worship Me). The first interpretation holds that the worship mentioned refers to the worship that will occur in the Hereafter necessarily, though obedience in this world is voluntary. The second interpretation is that the verse means God created them only to command them to worship, and the command itself is called worship due to its connection to the act. The author considers both interpretations valid, showing flexibility in understanding divine speech.

Key Terms

عبادة
تكليف
اضطرار
اختيار
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the verse only means physical worship in this life, and any other interpretation is invalid.
Correction: The passage shows that the verse can refer to the necessary worship in the Hereafter or to the command to worship, both valid interpretations within Islamic theology.

Checkpoint

B) Worship by angels or worship by humans
C) Worship in the afterlife necessarily, or the command to worship
D) Worship of God or worship of idols

Key Takeaway
The verse about creation for worship admits multiple valid interpretations, teaching us that divine speech can have layers of meaning.

God's Guidance and Human Choice: The Case of Thamud
Baqillani answers an objection about Thamud's misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani reconciles God's guidance with human rejection in the verse about Thamud.

Core Idea
God’s guidance does not force belief; humans can still choose to reject.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a question about a Quranic verse that seems to attribute misguidance to God. He offers two plausible interpretations, both preserving human responsibility. This lesson explores his careful exegesis.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and verse
Start by reading the Arabic passage and its translation. Note the objection about the verse on Thamud.
The verse is from Surah Fussilat or similar; focus on Baqillani's response.
2
Understand the first interpretation
Baqillani proposes that a group of Thamud initially believed and were guided, but later apostatized and chose blindness.
This interpretation maintains that guidance was effective for a time, but human free will led to rejection.
3
Understand the second interpretation
Alternatively, God guided one party of Thamud, while another party independently preferred blindness.
This reading highlights that the verse may refer to two distinct groups.
4
Examine the supporting verse
Baqillani cites another verse describing Thamud as two parties quarreling, which supports the second interpretation.
The supporting evidence reinforces that the Quran itself points to division among Thamud.
5
Reflect on the theological implications
Consider how both interpretations preserve human responsibility while affirming God's guidance.
This passage guards against the misconception that God forces misguidance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
إن سألوا فقالوا : ما معنى قوله : وأما ثمود فهديناهم فاستحبوا العمى على الهدى ؟ .
قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أن قوماً من أصحاب ثمود آمنوا فاهتدوا، ثم ارتدوا عن الإيمان وكفروا واستحبوا العمى على الهدى ويمكن أن يكون أراد أنه هدى فريقاً من ثمود فاستحب فريق آخر العمى على الهدى . لأن الله تعالى أخبر أنهم فريقان فقال عزّ من قائل : ولقد أرسلنا إلى ثمود أخاهم صالحاً أن اعبدوا الله فإذا هم فريقان يختصمون.
If they ask and say: What is the meaning of His saying: 'And as for Thamud, We guided them, but they preferred blindness over guidance'? It was said to them: The meaning of that is that a group of the people of Thamud believed and were guided, then they apostatized from faith and disbelieved and preferred blindness over guidance. And it is possible that He meant that He guided a party of Thamud, then another party preferred blindness over guidance. Because Allah Almighty informed that they were two parties, saying: 'And We sent to Thamud their brother Salih, saying: Worship Allah, and then they became two parties quarreling.'
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage answers an objection concerning the verse about Thamud, where God says He guided them yet they preferred blindness. The response provides two possible explanations: 1) A group of Thamud initially believed and were guided, but later apostatized and chose disbelief. 2) God guided one party, while another party rejected guidance. The support comes from another verse that describes two parties among Thamud. Thus, God's guidance does not force belief; human choice remains.

God's Creation of Love of Faith: Specific to Believers
Baqillani answers an objection about God creating love of faith and hate of disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani defends that God only creates love of faith in believers, not love of disbelief in disbelievers.

Core Idea
God's address in the Quran is specific to believers, not universal to all.

This passage tackles a common objection about divine decree: if God makes faith beloved to believers, does He also make disbelief beloved to disbelievers? Baqillani shows that the Quranic verse is addressed exclusively to believers, so it doesn't imply God creates love of disbelief. Understanding this distinction preserves God's justice while affirming His sovereignty.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and verse citation
Read the Arabic passage, noting how the objection quotes the verse (Quran 49:7) and challenges: how can God create love of faith in believers without also creating love of disbelief in disbelievers?
The objection assumes a universal application of the verse.
2
Identify Baqillani's answer
Baqillani responds by specifying that the verse is addressed only to believers, described as 'righteous' and 'rightly guided'. It does not refer to disbelievers or all responsible beings.
The key phrase is 'هذا خطاب من الله تعالى للمؤمنين'.
3
Reflect on the implication
Consider why this distinction matters: it affirms that God's creation of love of faith is specific to those He has guided, while disbelievers' love of disbelief stems from their own choice, not His creation.
This maintains God's justice and human accountability.

Why Humans Are Questioned Despite God Creating Their Actions
Baqillani answers an objection from Qur'an 21:23 by distinguishing creation and acquisition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses the distinction between creation and acquisition to reconcile divine omnipotence with human accountability.

Core Idea
God creates actions; humans acquire them and are responsible for what they acquire.

The Qur'an states that God is not questioned about what He does, but humans are questioned. How can this be if God creates everything, including human actions? Baqillani tackles this apparent contradiction by introducing a crucial distinction. Let's see how he resolves the objection with the concepts of creation and acquisition.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection
Start by reading the objection posed against the Ash'ari position. Understand the challenge: if humans do not truly create actions, why are they questioned?
The objectors assume that questioning implies independent action.
2
Analyze Baqillani's answer
Read the reply carefully. Notice the key distinction: God creates (yakhluq) and humans acquire (yaksibūn). The questioning applies to acquisition, not creation.
Acquisition (kasb) implies voluntary choice even though the action is created by God.
3
Reflect on the implications
Consider why God is not questioned: He has no superior imposing obligation. Humans, by contrast, have obligations regarding what they acquire.
This preserves divine sovereignty while maintaining human responsibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مسألة
فإن قالوا : فما معنى قوله عزّ وجلّ : لا يُسأل عما يفعل وهم يسألون ، وهم لم يفعلوا عندكم شيئاً؟ .
قيل لهم : معنى ذلك أنهم يُسألون عما يكسبون ولا يُسأل هو تعالى عما يخلق، لأنه لا آمر فوقه ولا تكليف عليه فيما يخلق، وعليهم الأمر والتكليف فيما يكسبون .
If they say: So what is the meaning of His saying, Mighty and Majestic: 'He is not questioned about what He does, but they are questioned', and according to you they do not do anything? It is said to them: The meaning of that is that they are questioned about what they acquire, and He, Exalted, is not questioned about what He creates, because there is no commander above Him and no obligation upon Him in what He creates, and upon them is the command and obligation in what they acquire.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage answers an objection based on Quran 21:23: if God creates all actions, why are humans questioned? The response introduces the key distinction between creation (khalq) and acquisition (kasb). God creates the actions, but humans acquire them voluntarily and are therefore responsible. God is not questioned because He is sovereign and has no superior imposing obligations on Him. The obligation and command apply only to humans regarding what they acquire.

Key Terms

يكسبون
يخلق
تكليف
أمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think that if God creates all actions, humans cannot be held responsible, making divine questioning unjust.
Correction: Baqillani explains that responsibility arises from acquisition (kasb), not creation (khalq). Humans voluntarily acquire actions that God creates, so they are rightfully questioned.

Checkpoint

B) Humans are questioned about what they acquire, not what God creates
C) God is questioned about His actions
D) The verse is only for non-believers

Key Takeaway
God creates actions, but humans acquire them and are accountable for their acquisition, reconciling divine sovereignty with human responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

The Objection from Divine Verses: Does God Create Evil?
Baqillani presents an objection using Quran 4:79 and begins to refute it.

This passage presents a classic objection against the Ash'ari position that God creates all actions, using the Quranic verse that distinguishes between good from God and evil from oneself. Why Mu'tazila are Called Qadariyyah and the True Meaning of Qadr
Baqillani explains the naming of Qadariyyah and defines qadr via al-Khattabi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila are called Qadariyyah and what the true meaning of divine decree (qadr) is according to Sunni scholars.

Core Idea
The Mu'tazila are called Qadariyyah because they deny divine decree by claiming to create their own actions.

Baqillani begins by addressing a common question: why do Sunni scholars label the Mu'tazila as Qadariyyah? The answer reveals a fundamental disagreement about the nature of human action and divine power. He then clarifies, through al-Khattabi, what qadr really means — not compulsion, but God's prior knowledge and creation of all actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Notice the rhetorical structure: a question from the Mu'tazila and the Sunni answer.
The passage includes a quote from al-Khattabi, so pay attention to the shift.
2
Understand the accusation against Mu'tazila
The passage states that Mu'tazila claim to create their own actions and be independent in power. This is the basis for calling them Qadariyyah.
3
Grasp al-Khattabi's correction
Al-Khattabi explains that qadr does not mean compulsion; rather, it is about God's prior knowledge and His creation of all actions, good and evil.
This corrects a common misunderstanding.
4
Note the lexical meaning of qadr
The passage gives linguistic explanations: qadr can refer to an action measured out, and the word can be pronounced with tashdid or without.
5
Reflect on the overall message
The final sentence of this lesson's passage declares that every event depends on God's power and will. This is the core Sunni belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب في وجوب تسميتهم قدرية فإن قالوا: فلِمَ سميتمونا قدريَّة؟ قيل لهم : لادّعائكم لأنفسكم الكذب الذي لا أصل له من خلق أعمالكم وتقديرها والتفرد بملكها والقدرة لما صدر عن قال الخطابي أبو سليمان رحمه الله : يتوهم كثير من الناس أن معنی القدر من الله ، والقضاء منه الإجبار والقهر للعبد على ما قضاه وقدره وليس كذلك وإنما معناه الإخبار عن تقدم علم الله بما يكون من أفعال العباد واكتسابها وصدورها عن تقدير منه وخلقه لها خيرها وشرها . ا . هـ . والقدر قد يطلق على ما صدر مقدراً عن فعل القادر كالهدم والقبض أو بسم فعل الهادم والقابض. ويقال : قدرت الشيء وبتخفيف الدال وتشديدها بمعنى واحد. والمعنى أن كل حادث من خير وشر ونفع وضرر فهو مستند إلى قدرته وإرادته . قال الله تعالى: (إنا كل شيء خلقناه بقدر). ويقول أيضاً: (وخلق كل شيء فقدره تقديراً). وقال: (وما أصابكم يوم التقى الجمعان فبإذن الله) أي بقضاء الله وقدره. وأيضاً (ما أصاب من مصيبة في الأرض ولا في أنفسكم إلا في كتاب من قبل أن نبرأها) وقال: (ونبلوكم بالشر والخير فتنة) وقوله: (وإذا أراد الله بقوم سوءاً فلا مرد له) وفي صحيح مسلم كل شيء بقدر حتى العجز والكيس. ثم قال الزركشي : وهو من لوازم القول بخلق الأفعال كلها». وهي مسألة القضاء والقدر التي لا يتم الإيمان إلا به أن يعتقد أن كل شيء من الطاعة والعصيان والنفع والضر بمشيئة الله خلافاً للمعتزلة، فإنهم يعتقدون أن أمر بمشيئة العبد مستقل به من غير سبق قضاء وقدر ولذلك قيل لهم القدرية لأنهم نفوا القدر .
Section on the necessity of calling them Qadariyyah. If they say: Why do you call us Qadariyyah? It is said to them: Due to your claim for yourselves — which is a lie with no basis — of creating your actions, and estimating them, and being unique in their ownership and power. [Then] Al-Khattabi Abu Sulayman (may God have mercy on him) said: Many people mistakenly think that the meaning of decree from God, and predestination from Him, is compulsion and coercion of the servant to what He decreed and predestined. It is not so; rather its meaning is informing of the precedence of God's knowledge of what will be from the actions of servants, their acquisition, and their issuance from an estimation from Him and His creation of them, their good and their evil. End. And 'qadr' may be applied to what issues as measured from the action of the capable one, like demolition and grasping, or by the name of the action of the demolisher and the grasper. It is said: 'qadartu al-shay' and with tashdid of the dal both mean the same. The meaning is that every event, good or evil, benefit or harm, is dependent on His power and will. God Most High said: 'Indeed, all things We created with predestination.' And He also says: 'And created all things and determined them with precise determination.' And He said: 'And what afflicted you on the day the two armies met was by the permission of God' i.e., by God's decree and predestination. And also: 'No disaster strikes upon the earth or among yourselves except that it is in a register before We bring it into being.' And He said: 'And We test you with evil and good as trial.' And His saying: 'And when God intends for a people evil, there is no repelling it.' And in Sahih Muslim: 'Everything is by predestination, even incapacity and intelligence.' Then al-Zarkashi said: 'And it is one of the necessary consequences of the doctrine of the creation of all actions.' And this is the matter of al-qada' and al-qadr, faith is not complete except by believing that everything — obedience and disobedience, benefit and harm — is by the will of God, contrary to the Mu'tazila, for they believe that the matter is by the will of the servant, independent of it without preceding qada' and qadr. Therefore they were called Qadariyyah because they denied al-qadr.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof section. It begins with the 'باب' heading explaining why the Mu'tazila are called Qadariyyah: because they falsely claim to create their own actions and be independent in power. Then Baqillani (through a quotation from al-Khattabi) clarifies that the true meaning of qadr from God is not compulsion but the precedence of God's knowledge and the fact that all actions—good and evil—are created by God and known before they occur. Al-Khattabi stresses that people misunderstand qadr as coercion; rather it is about God's knowledge and creation. Then follows a lexical explanation of qadr, and Quranic verses and hadith supporting that everything is by God's determination. Finally, al-Zarkashi adds that the Mu'tazila denied qadr by claiming the servant is independent in his actions, which is why they are called Qadariyyah (the deniers of qadr). The section concludes that faith requires belief that all things are by God's will, contrary to the Mu'tazila who attribute independent power to the servant.

Key Terms
القدرية (Qadariyyah)
القدر (divine decree)
القضاء (divine predestination)
خلق الأعمال (creation of actions)
المشيئة (will)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyyah are those who believe in qadr most strongly.
Correction: They are called Qadariyyah because they deny qadr, claiming independent creation of actions.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani say the Mu'tazila are called Qadariyyah?
A) Because they affirm qadr most strongly
B) Because they deny qadr by claiming they create their own actions
C) Because they follow Qadr ibn Saif
D) Because they reject all qadr verses

Key Takeaway
The Mu'tazila are named Qadariyyah because they deny divine decree by attributing the creation of their actions to themselves.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you do a good deed, do you feel a sense of pride as if you alone produced it, or do you acknowledge that God created both the action and the ability? How can you cultivate the latter attitude daily?
?
If qadr does not mean God compels you, then why do you sometimes blame destiny for your sins? What would change if you truly believed every event depends on His power and will while still holding yourself accountable?
?
Al-Khattabi says many mistakenly think qadr is coercion. Have you ever felt resentful toward God when things went wrong, as if He forced you into a bad situation? How does this lesson correct that feeling in your heart?

Divine Decree

Quranic and Hadith Evidence for Qadr
Baqillani provides scriptural evidence and concludes the Sunni doctrine of qadr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural proofs that everything is by God's decree and why this belief is essential for faith.

Core Idea
The Quran and hadith confirm that all events, good and evil, occur by God's decree.

After clarifying the meaning of qadr, Baqillani provides the scriptural foundation. He cites several Quranic verses and a hadith to demonstrate that all things — from creation to daily events — are determined by God's power and will. He then concludes that the Mu'tazila's denial of this is why they are called Qadariyyah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Quranic verses cited
The passage quotes multiple verses: 'Indeed, all things We created with predestination', 'And created all things and determined them', and others. Read each one and note how they support the doctrine.
The verses cover creation, historical events, and personal trials.
2
Analyze the hadith
The hadith from Sahih Muslim states 'Everything is by predestination, even incapacity and intelligence.' Reflect on its comprehensive scope.
This hadith reinforces that even human abilities are decreed.
3
Understand al-Zarkashi's comment
Al-Zarkashi says belief in qadr is a necessary consequence of the doctrine that all actions are created by God.
This ties the proof back to the earlier discussion.
4
Grasp the conclusion
The passage ends by stating that faith requires believing everything is by God's will, contrary to the Mu'tazila, and that this is why they are called Qadariyyah (deniers of qadr).

Divine Decree

Understanding Qadr: Allah's Knowledge and Creation of Actions
Al-Khattabi defines Qadr and refutes both misconception and Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the correct meaning of Qadr as Allah's prior knowledge and creation of all actions, and why this is a necessary part of faith.

Core Idea
Qadr is not compulsion; it is Allah's perfect knowledge and creation of all that occurs.

Many people mistakenly think that Qadr means Allah forces people to act. In this passage, Al-Khattabi clarifies the true meaning, linking it to Allah's prior knowledge and His creation of everything, both good and evil. This lesson will unpack his definition and its implications for faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation, noting Al-Khattabi's correction of the common misconception.
Pay attention to how he contrasts compulsion vs. knowledge.
2
Understand the definition of Qadr
Al-Khattabi says Qadr means 'informing about Allah's prior knowledge' and that actions occur from His determination and creation. Grasp that Qadr is about divine knowledge and power, not coercion.
3
Consider the linguistic usage
He notes that 'qadr' can also apply to actions that are determined. Reflect on how language and theology intersect.
4
Examine the scriptural evidence
He cites Quranic verses and a hadith to support that everything is by Allah's decree. See how he uses revelation to ground his definition.
5
Contrast with the Mu'tazila view
Al-Zarkashi concludes that the correct belief is against the Mu'tazila who deny Qadr. Understand why this distinction matters for faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الخطابي أبو سليمان رحمه الله: يتوهم كثير من الناس أن معنى القدر من الله، والقضاء منه الإجبار والقهر للعبد على ما قضاه وقدره، وليس كذلك، وإنما معناه الإخبار عن تقدم علم الله بما يكون من أفعال العباد واكتسابها وصدورها عن تقدير منه وخلقه لها خيرها وشرها. والقدر قد يطلق على ما صدر مقدراً عن فعل القادر كالهدم والقبض أو بسم فعل الهادم والقابض. ويقال: قدرت الشيء بتخفيف الدال وتشديدها بمعنى واحد. والمعنى أن كل حادث من خير وشر ونفع وضرر فهو مستند إلى قدرته وإرادته. قال الله تعالى: {إنا كل شيء خلقناه بقدر}. ويقول أيضاً: {وخلق كل شيء فقدره تقديراً}. وقال: {وما أصابكم يوم التقى الجمعان فبإذن الله} أي بقضاء الله وقدره. وأيضاً {ما أصاب من مصيبة في الأرض ولا في أنفسكم إلا في كتاب من قبل أن نبرأها} وقال: {ونبلوكم بالشر والخير فتنة} وقوله: {وإذا أراد الله بقوم سوءاً فلا مرد له}. وفي صحيح مسلم: كل شيء بقدر حتى العجز والكيس. ثم قال الزركشي: وهو من لوازم القول بخلق الأفعال كلها. وهي مسألة القضاء والقدر التي لا يتم الإيمان إلا به أن يعتقد أن كل شيء من الطاعة والعصيان والنفع والضر بمشيئة الله خلافاً للمعتزلة، فإنهم يعتقدون أن الأمر بمشيئة العبد مستقل به من غير سبق قضاء وقدر، ولذلك قيل لهم القدرية لأنهم نفوا القدر.
Al-Khattabi Abu Sulayman, may Allah have mercy on him, said: Many people mistakenly think that the meaning of Qadr from Allah, and al-Qada', is compulsion and coercion of the servant over what He decreed and determined. That is not so. Rather, its meaning is informing about Allah's prior knowledge of what will happen from the actions of the servants, their acquisition, and their occurrence due to a determination from Him and His creation of them, both their good and their evil. And al-Qadr may be applied to that which is issued as determined from the act of the capable, like demolition and holding, or it is used for the act of the demolisher and the holder. And it is said: qadartu al-shay'a with the dāl unvoiced and doubled with one meaning. The meaning is that every event, good and evil, benefit and harm, is attributable to His power and will. Allah the Exalted said: 'Indeed, all things We created with Qadr.' And He also said: 'And He created everything and determined it with determination.' And He said: 'And what struck you on the day the two armies met was by the permission of Allah,' meaning by Allah's decree and Qadr. And also: 'No disaster strikes the earth or among yourselves except that it is in a Book before We bring it into being.' And He said: 'And We test you with evil and good as trial.' And His saying: 'And when Allah intends evil for a people, there is no repelling it.' And in Sahih Muslim: 'Everything is by Qadr, even incapacity and cleverness.' Then al-Zarkashi said: And it is among the necessary implications of the statement that all actions are created. And it is the issue of al-Qada' and al-Qadr, which faith is not complete except by believing that everything—obedience, disobedience, benefit, harm—is by the will of Allah, contrary to the Mu'tazila, for they believe that the affair is by the will of the servant, independent of it, without prior Qada' and Qadr. Therefore, they were called Qadariyya because they denied Qadr.
Source pages p. 366

Commentary
This passage is an extended definition and clarification of the concept of Qadr by Al-Khattabi. He begins by correcting a common misunderstanding: people think Qadr means Allah compels people to act. He says it actually refers to Allah's prior knowledge and creation of all actions, including their acquisition by humans. He then gives a linguistic definition: 'qadr' can mean the act of determining something. He emphasizes that every event, good or bad, is under Allah's power and will. He supports with Quranic verses and a hadith. Then al-Zarkashi adds that this entails that all actions are created by Allah. The passage concludes that faith requires belief that everything is by Allah's will, contrary to the Mu'tazila who grant independent will to humans, hence they are called Qadariyya for denying Qadr.

Key Terms
قدر
قضاء
خلق الأفعال
المعتزلة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Qadr means Allah compels people to act against their will.
Correction: Al-Khattabi explains that Qadr refers to Allah's prior knowledge and creation of actions, not coercion.

Checkpoint
According to Al-Khattabi, what is the correct meaning of Qadr from Allah?
A) Compulsion and coercion of the servant
B) Informing about Allah's prior knowledge and creation of actions
C) The servant's independent power
D) The absence of predestination

Key Takeaway
Qadr is Allah's comprehensive knowledge and creation of all things, not compulsion, and believing this is essential to faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or sin, do you ever feel it was 'written' so you are helpless? How does knowing that Qadr is Allah's knowledge – not compulsion – remind you of your accountability and your need to repent and strive? What will you do the next time you are tempted to blame fate for your shortcomings?
?
This lesson contrasts the belief that everything is by Allah's will with the Mu'tazila view of independent human will. Is there an area of your life where you insist on being 'in control' and resist submitting to Allah's decree? How can you practice deeper trust in Allah's wisdom while still using the free will He gave you to obey Him?
?
If you truly internalize that even your incapacity and cleverness are from Allah (as the hadith says), does that make you more grateful for your abilities and more humble in your failures? Or do you still pride yourself on your achievements? How can you train your heart to attribute all outcomes to Allah alone starting today?

Divine Decree
beginner

Divine Knowledge and Will: Abu Hanifa's Argument
Abu Hanifa poses two sequential questions to Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Abu Hanifa Maturidi uses a logical two-step question to refute the Qadariyya by linking God's eternal knowledge and His will to execute it.

Core Idea
If God knows all things, He must will them; denying this implies ignorance of His will.

In this passage, Abu Hanifa Maturidi presents a concise yet powerful argument against the Qadariyya who deny divine predestination. He asks two sequential questions: first about God's knowledge of all that happens, then about His will to actualize that knowledge. The answers force the Qadariyya to either admit God's comprehensive will or fall into blasphemy.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then the translation. Notice the two questions and their implied consequences.
This passage is the opening salvo of Abu Hanifa's refutation.
2
Identify the two questions
The first question is about God's knowledge: 'Did Allah know what will be?' The second is about His will: 'Did He will to execute His knowledge?' See how they build on each other.
3
Analyze the logical consequences
If Qadariyya deny the first question, they disbelieve by ignoring God's omniscience. If they accept it but deny the second, they imply God willed ignorance, which is unwise. Only accepting both leads to affirming divine decree.
This shows the power of logical necessity in kalam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقال أبو حنيفة رحمه الله الإمام أبو منصور الماتريدي: بيننا وبين القدرية الكلام في حرفين: أن نسألهم هل علم الله ما يكون أبداً على ما يكون؟ فإن قالوا لا كفروا لأنهم جهلوا ربهم. وإن قالوا نعم قيل: شاء أن ينفذ علمه كما علم أولاً؟ فإن قالوا لا قالوا بأن الله شاء أن يكون جاهلاً ومن شاء ذلك فليس بحكيم. وإن قالوا نعم أقروا بأنه شاء أن يكون كل شيء كما علم أن يكون. ثم قال: فإن قال قائل: إذا قبح الأمر بالمعاصي لم لا قبح إرادة كونها؟ قيل لأوجه: أحدها التناقض في الأمر وليس ذلك في الإرادة لأن الفعل ربما يصير للأمر فمحال الأمر بالمعصية لأنه يصير بالأمر طاعة فيبطل معنى المعصية، بها الأمر ليست الإرادة كذلك ألا ترى أن كل ما يمل مختار مريد لفعله ومحال أن يقال إنه أمر نفسه بفعله ثبت أنهما مختلفان. قال: وأيضاً إن الله يوصف بالإرادة في فعله ومحال أن يكون عليه أمر فيه فثبت أن أحد الوجهين ليس هو دليل الآخر.
And Abu Hanifa—may Allah have mercy on him, the Imam Abu Mansur al-Maturidi—said: Between us and the Qadariyya is discussion on two points: that we ask them: Did Allah know what will be eternally as it will be? If they say no, they disbelieved because they ignored their Lord. And if they say yes, it is said: Did He will to execute His knowledge as He knew originally? If they say no, they have said that Allah willed to be ignorant, and whoever wills that is not wise. And if they say yes, they have affirmed that He willed everything to be as He knew it would be. Then he said: If it is said: When commanding disobedience is evil, why is willing its occurrence not evil? It is said for several aspects: One of them is the contradiction in command, and that is not in will, because an action may become due to command, so commanding disobedience is impossible because it becomes obedience by command, nullifying the meaning of disobedience. The command is not will likewise—do you not see that everything one does, one is a chooser willing his action, and it is impossible to say that he commanded himself to do it. Thus it is established that they are different. He said: And also Allah is described with will in His action, and it is impossible that He be commanded in it. So it is established that one of the two aspects is not a proof for the other.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage is a logical refutation. Abu Hanifa Maturidi presents two points of argument: first, concerning God's knowledge—if Qadariyya admit God knows all things, they must also admit that He wills to execute that knowledge, meaning everything occurs as He knows. If they deny His will, they imply God is ignorant. Second, they object: if commanding evil is evil, why is willing evil not evil? The answer distinguishes between command and will: a command makes an act become obedience, but will does not. God's will is related to His own action, and no one commands Him. Thus the objection fails.

Key Terms
علم الله
مشيئة الله

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that Qadariyya accept God's knowledge but deny His will, yet this is a tenable position.
Correction: The argument shows that denying God's will to execute His knowledge leads to attributing ignorance to God, which is absurd and blasphemous. Thus, accepting God's knowledge logically entails accepting His will for all things.

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the consequence if the Qadariyya deny that Allah willed to execute His knowledge?
A) They become Muslims
B) They have said that Allah willed to be ignorant
C) They are still believers but mistaken
D) They must accept human free will

Key Takeaway
To refute predestination denial, Abu Hanifa shows that affirming God's knowledge necessitates affirming His will to execute it, or else one implies God's ignorance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If you truly believe that Allah knows and wills everything that happens, how does that change the way you react to setbacks in your life? Are you able to accept them as part of His will, or do you sometimes secretly question His wisdom? What would it take for you to completely surrender to that truth?
?
The Qadariyya's denial of God's will was rooted in a desire to protect human freedom. Where in your own heart do you resist submitting to God's decree because you want to maintain control? What is holding you back from affirming that His will is good even when it contradicts your plans?
?
Abu Hanifa's argument exposes the logical contradiction in denying God's will while affirming His knowledge. Is there any area of your life where you intellectually affirm something about Allah but your actions or emotions betray a denial of it? What would it look like to align your heart with what you know to be true about His will?

Command vs. Will: Answering the Qadariyya Objection
Abu Hanifa refutes an objection by distinguishing command from will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why commanding evil is evil but willing its occurrence is not, based on the essential difference between command and will.

Core Idea
Command changes an act's moral status; will does not, so God willing sin is not evil.

A key objection from the Qadariyya is that if God wills sins, He would be commanding evil. Abu Hanifa responds by distinguishing between command (amr) and will (irada). He shows that a command transforms an act into obedience, whereas will does not have that effect. This distinction safeguards God's justice while affirming His absolute will.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Qadariyya objection and Abu Hanifa's reply. Notice the key terms 'command' and 'will'.
2
Identify the core distinction
The key insight: a command makes an act become obedience, so commanding disobedience is contradictory. But willing an act does not change its nature; thus, willing sin is not the same as commanding it.
This is the logical pivot of the argument.
3
Apply the distinction
Reflect on how this answers the objection: God's will for sins to occur does not imply He approves of them or commands them. His will is related to His own action, while command is directed to others.
This preserves divine wisdom and justice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If they say no, they have said that Allah willed to be ignorant, and whoever wills that is not wise. And if they say yes, they have affirmed that He willed everything to be as He knew it would be. Thus it is established that they are different. He said: And also Allah is described with will in His action, and it is impossible that He be commanded in it. So it is established that one of the two aspects is not a proof for the other.

Key Terms
الأمر

قبح

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Many assume that command and will are identical in God, so willing sin would be as evil as commanding it.
Correction: The passage shows they are distinct: command changes an act's moral status (making it obedience), while will does not. God's will for sin is not a command to sin, so no evil is implied.

Frequent Mention of Qadr Does Not Merit Blame
Baqillani answers the objection that frequent qadr talk makes one Qadari.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Ash'aris' frequent discussion of qadr does not make them Qadari, and how Baqillani refutes the objection by distinguishing truthful speech from false claims.

Core Idea
Truthful speech about qadr is not blameworthy; false claims earn the name.

Having presented the objection that the Ash'aris' frequent talk of qadr should label them Qadari, Baqillani now delivers a crisp rebuttal. He flips the argument: the truthful person does not inherit a blameworthy name, while those who falsely claim self-determination deserve it. This lesson unpacks that exchange and clarifies the true criterion for being a Qadari.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the full Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how the opponents' accusation is structured and Baqillani's response.
2
Identify the key distinction
Baqillani distinguishes between truthful mention (which does not incur blame) and false claim (which does). Find where he makes this contrast.
3
Analyze the counter-argument
Notice how Baqillani turns the tables: if people were asked who the Qadariyya are, they would point to the opponents, not to the Ash'aris. This is a rhetorical and logical move.
4
Reflect on the summary
The passage ends by defining a Qadari as one who attributes false beliefs to qadr. Reflect on how this definition resolves the objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: فأنتم تكثرون ذكر القدر والقول بأن كل شيء قضاء وقدر، فيجب لزوم هذا الاسم لكم. قيل لهم: نحن محقون في هذا القول، ولا يلزم المحق اسم الذم. وأنتم تكثرون ذكر تقديركم لأفعالكم وتفرُّدكم بملكها وخلقها وتكذبون وتفترون في هذه الدعوى، فوجب لزوم الاسم لكم. على أنه لو جميع الفرق وعامة الناس وخاصتهم عن القدرية، لم يرشدوا إلا إليكم دون كل فرقة من فرق الأمة. وجملة هذا القول أن قدرياً سئل نسبة إلى القول بالباطل في القدر.
If they say: You frequently mention al-qadr and the statement that everything is by decree and predestination, so this name must apply to you. It is said to them: We are truthful in this statement, and the truthful person does not incur the blameworthy name. But you frequently mention your own measuring of your actions and your exclusive possession and creation of them, and you lie and fabricate in this claim, so the name must apply to you. Moreover, if all the sects and the common and elite people were asked about the Qadariyya, they would point only to you, to the exclusion of every other sect of the community. The summary of this statement is that a Qadari is asked regarding attribution to the false statement concerning al-qadr.
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage presents the second objection: the opponents argue that since the Ash'aris frequently mention qadr and qada', they should be called Qadariyya. The answer is that frequency of truthful mention does not incur blame; rather, it is the false claim of measuring and creating actions that merits the name. Furthermore, if all people were asked who the Qadariyya are, they would point to the opponents. The final sentence summarizes: the Qadari is one who holds false beliefs about qadr.

Key Terms
قضاء (qada')
قدر (qadr)
تقدير (taqdir)
قدري (Qadari)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that merely speaking about predestination makes one a Qadari.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that the key is the content of the belief: truthful mention of qadr does not earn blame; it is the false claim of self-determination that merits the label.

Checkpoint
According to al-Baqillani, why does frequent mention of qadr not make one a Qadari?
A) Because the Qadari is one who denies qadr.
B) Because the truthful mention is not blameworthy.
C) Because the Ash'aris only mention it rarely.
D) Because the name only applies to non-Muslims.

Key Takeaway
A Qadari is defined not by frequency of discussing qadr, but by holding false beliefs about it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

God's Decree of Sin: Not a Command
Answers whether God decrees sins by distinguishing meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that when Muslims say God decrees sins, they mean He creates them according to His will, not that He commands them.

Core Idea
God's decree of sin is creative, not legislative.

A common objection is that if God decrees sins, He must be commanding evil. The early scholar answers by distinguishing two meanings of qada: creation and command. This lesson unpacks that vital distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the question assumes that 'qada' implies command. The answer clarifies that qada here means creation.
The phrase 'على معنى أنه خلق' is key.
2
Identify the two meanings of qada
The answer explicitly contrasts qada as creation (خلق) with qada as command (أمر). Understand that both are valid but context determines which is intended.
3
Apply the distinction
Reflect on why this distinction matters: it preserves God's justice while affirming His absolute will and power over all things, including sins.
This answers a major theological objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال قائل: أفتقولون إن الله تعالى قضى المعاصي وقدرها كما أنه خلقها وأوجدها؟ قيل له: أجل، نقول ذلك على معنى أنه خلق العصيان وجعله على حسب قصده ولا نقول إنه قضى بذلك بمعنى أنه أمر به. مسألة: فإن قيل: فعلى كم وجه ينقسم القضاء؟ قيل له: على وجوه. منها القضاء بمعنى الخلق. قال الله تعالى: فقضاهن سبع سموات في يومين يعني: خلقهن. وقال تعالى: فلما قضينا عليه الموت، يعني: خلقناه وأوجدناه به. وقد يكون القضاء بمعنى الإخبار والكتابة والإعلام، وكذلك القدر. قال الله عز وجل: وقضينا إلى بني إسرائيل في الكتاب لتفسدن في الأرض مرتين، أي: أعلمناهم ذلك وأخبرناهم به. وقال في القدر بمعنى التقدير: وقدر فيها أقواتها. والقدر أيضاً بمعنى الخلق. ومنه قوله تعالى: قدر فهدى. وقد يكون القضاء بمعنى الأمر. قال الله عز وجل: وقضى ربك ألا تعبدوا إلا إياه، أي: أمر ربك.
If a questioner says: 'Do you say that God Almighty decreed (qada) sins and predetermined them (qadarahā) just as He created them and brought them into existence?' It is said to him: Yes, we say that in the sense that He created disobedience and made it according to His intent, and we do not say that He decreed that in the sense that He commanded it. An issue: If it is said: 'On how many aspects is al-qada divided?' It is said to him: On aspects. Among them: al-qada in the sense of creation. God Almighty said: 'Then He completed them (qadāhunna) as seven heavens in two days'—meaning He created them. And He said: 'When We decreed (qadaynā) death upon him'—meaning We created him and brought him into existence by it. And al-qada may be in the sense of informing, writing, and making known, and likewise al-qadar. God Almighty said: 'And We decreed (qadaynā) to the Children of Israel in the Book: You will surely cause corruption on the earth twice'—meaning We made that known to them and informed them of it. And He said concerning al-qadar in the sense of estimation: 'And He estimated (qaddara) therein its provisions.' And al-qadar also has the meaning of creation. Among that is His saying: 'He determined (qadara) and guided.' And al-qada may be in the sense of command. God Almighty said: 'And your Lord has decreed (qada) that you worship none but Him'—meaning your Lord commanded.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer format followed by an enumeration of the meanings of qada and qadar. It begins with a question: 'Do you say that God decrees (qada) and predetermines (qadar) sins just as He creates them?' The answer affirms this but clarifies the meaning: God creates disobedience and makes it according to His intent (qasd), not as a command (amr). That is, His decree of sin is a creative decree, not a legislative command. Then a new question asks on how many aspects (wujuh) qada is divided. The answer gives multiple senses: (1) Qada as creation (khalq), supported by Quranic verses where 'qada' is interpreted as 'creating'. (2) Qada as informing (ikhbar), writing (kitaba), and making known (i'lam), citing the verse to the Children of Israel. (3) Qadar as estimation (taqdir), as in the verse about provisions. (4) Qadar also as creation (khalq), as in 'qadara fahada' (He determined and guided). (5) Qada as command (amr), as in the verse about worshipping none but Him. The lesson thus distinguishes these meanings to prevent confusion: when speaking of God's decree of sin, it is not a command but a creative act.

Key Terms
قضاء
قدر
خلق
أمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God decrees sins, He commands them, making Him unjust.
Correction: The passage clarifies that God's decree of sin is His creation of it, not a command. He creates sins as part of His plan, but He prohibits them by His command.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, in what sense does God decree sins?
A) As a command
B) As a creation
C) As a suggestion
D) As a divine approval

Key Takeaway
God's decree of sin is creative, not commanding — He creates sin according to His will but forbids it by His law.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you ever catch yourself thinking, 'It was decreed so it's not really my fault'? How does today's lesson force you to own your sin without shifting blame to God? What concrete step will you take next time you are tempted to use qadar as an excuse?
?
Is there a sin you have been excusing because you assumed God must approve since He willed it? How does the distinction between creative decree and command change your view of that sin? Will you repent with full accountability starting now?
?
Do you truly believe God is just despite the existence of evil? How does knowing that He only creates sin but does not command it help you trust His justice? What will you do today to submit to His commands, even when your desires contradict them?

The Multiple Meanings of Qada and Qadar
Enumerates meanings of qada and qadar with Quranic evidence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and recognize the different meanings of qada and qadar as used in the Quran and theology.

Core Idea
Qada and qadar have multiple meanings: creation, informing, estimation, and command.

The same Arabic terms can carry different senses depending on context. This lesson shows you how early scholars classified the meanings of qada and qadar with Quranic examples, preventing confusion in theological discussions.

Guided Path
1
Read the enumeration passage
Start by reading the Arabic passage where the teacher lists the meanings of qada and qadar. Notice the Quranic proofs for each meaning.
2
Identify the categories
The passage gives five distinct meanings: qada as creation, qada as informing/writing, qadar as estimation, qadar as creation, and qada as command. Find each one.
Some overlap, like qada and qadar both meaning creation.
3
Match each meaning to its Quranic example
For each meaning, note the verse cited. Understand how the same word is interpreted differently based on context.
This trains you in tafsir and theological lexicon.
4
Reflect on the importance
Consider why this classification matters: it prevents misreading verses and enables precise theological argumentation about divine will and action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

If a questioner says: 'Do you say that God Almighty decreed (qada) sins and predetermined them (qadarahā) just as He created them and brought them into existence?' It is said to him: Yes, we say that in the sense that He created disobedience and made it according to His intent, and we do not say that He decreed that in the sense that He commanded it. An issue: If it is said: 'On how many aspects is al-qada divided?' It is said to him: On aspects. Among them: al-qada in the sense of creation. God Almighty said: 'Then He completed them (qadāhunna) as seven heavens in two days'—meaning He created them. And He said: 'When We decreed (qadaynā) death upon him'—meaning We created him and brought him into existence by it. And al-qada may be in the sense of informing, writing, and making known, and likewise al-qadar. God Almighty said: 'And We decreed (qadaynā) to the Children of Israel in the Book: You will surely cause corruption on the earth twice'—meaning We made that known to them and informed them of it. And He said concerning al-qadar in the sense of estimation: 'And He estimated (qaddara) therein its provisions.' And al-qadar also has the meaning of creation. Among that is His saying: 'He determined (qadara) and guided.' And al-qada may be in the sense of command. God Almighty said: 'And your Lord has decreed (qada) that you worship none but Him'—meaning your Lord commanded.
Source pages p. 370

Commentary
This passage presents an objection-and-answer format followed by an enumeration of the meanings of qada and qadar. It begins with a question: 'Do you say that God decrees (qada) and predetermines (qadar) sins just as He creates them?' The answer affirms this but clarifies the meaning: God creates disobedience and makes it according to His intent (qasd), not as a command (amr). That is, His decree of sin is a creative decree, not a legislative command. Then a new question asks on how many aspects (wujuh) qada is divided. The answer gives multiple senses: (1) Qada as creation (khalq), supported by Quranic verses where 'qada' is interpreted as 'creating'. (2) Qada as informing (ikhbar), writing (kitaba), and making known (i'lam), citing the verse to the Children of Israel. (3) Qadar as estimation (taqdir), as in the verse about provisions. (4) Qadar also as creation (khalq), as in 'qadara fahada' (He determined and guided). (5) Qada as command (amr), as in the verse about worshipping none but Him. The lesson thus distinguishes these meanings to prevent confusion: when speaking of God's decree of sin, it is not a command but a creative act.

Key Terms
قضاء
قدر
خلق
إخبار
كتابة
تقدير
أمر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the verse 'Wa qada rabbuka alla ta'budu illa iyyah', what does 'qada' mean according to the passage?
A) Creation
B) Informing
C) Command
D) Estimation

Key Takeaway
Qada and qadar have multiple meanings; context determines whether they refer to creation, information, estimation, or command.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a hardship, do you instinctively think of qada as a command you must suffer through, or as a creation that God brings about with wisdom? How might that shift your patience?
?
The verse 'And your Lord has decreed that you worship none but Him' uses qada as a command. Are you treating God's command as a mere suggestion or as a binding decree that demands your entire life?
?
If qada and qadar can mean different things, have you been projecting a limited understanding onto God's actions in your life? What would change if you saw His decree as also an act of creation and information, not just command?

Pleasure with Divine Decree: Two Answers
Baqillani answers whether one must be pleased with God's decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's nuanced answer on being pleased with divine decree, distinguishing between what we must accept and what we are forbidden to approve.

Core Idea
Pleasure with decree means accepting God's commands, not approving forbidden things.

This passage deals with a subtle theological question: are believers required to be pleased with everything God decrees? Baqillani offers a careful answer that balances submission to God's will with moral responsibility. His response clarifies what 'pleasure with decree' actually means, helping Muslims avoid misunderstanding.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation to get the overall argument. Notice the question-and-answer format.
2
Identify the two answers
The passage gives two distinct answers: a specific one that distinguishes between commanded and forbidden, and a general one of unconditional pleasure.
3
Understand the distinction
In the first answer, Baqillani distinguishes between God's decree as creation (which He commands us to be pleased with) and what He forbids. We are not pleased with sin, even though God decrees it.
This is the key nuance.
4
Reflect on the implications
How does this balance between submission and moral responsibility work? Consider that we accept God's overall plan while still actively obeying His commands.
5
Address the common misunderstanding
How does this passage correct the idea that being pleased with decree means approving all evil? Note the explicit exclusion of forbidden things.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage gives two answers to the question of whether one should be pleased with God's decree. The first answer distinguishes: we are pleased with God's decree in the sense of creation, meaning we accept the created realities He commands us to will and be pleased with, such as obedience. But we are not pleased with what He forbids us to be pleased with, such as sin. The believer does not run ahead of God or object to His judgment. The second answer is more comprehensive: we are pleased with God's decree in general, in all circumstances, implying an unconditional acceptance of divine will. This balances active moral responsibility with ultimate submission to God's overarching plan.

The Two Meanings of Qada and Its Relation to the Decreed Thing
Baqillani defines two meanings of qada and resolves the identity question.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the term qada (decree) has two distinct meanings in kalam—creation versus obligation—and that its identity with the decreed thing depends on which meaning is used.

Core Idea
Qada is not always the same as its object—it depends on the meaning.

This passage from Baqillani tackles a crucial distinction in the theology of qada and qadar. Before we can discuss God's decree, we must clarify what the word 'decree' itself means. Baqillani shows that it can refer either to the act of creation (which is identical to what is created) or to a command/obligation (which is distinct from its object). Understanding this distinction prevents confusion in predestination debates.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Carefully read the Arabic passage and its English translation. Note the two different uses of qada that Baqillani introduces.
Pay attention to the phrase 'إلا على معنى أنه فرضها وأمر بها' – this is the key exception.
2
Identify the objector's question
Find the question 'فالقضاء عندكم هو المقضي أو غيره؟' and notice how it frames the issue: is the decree identical to its object or something else?
3
Understand the two-part answer
Baqillani answers that qada has two senses: creation (identical to the created thing) and obligation/notification (distinct from its object). Recognize the analogies: command vs. commanded, report vs. reported.
The exception 'إذا لم يكن خبراً عن نفسه' shows a subtle case where a report can be identical to its object.
4
Reflect on the implications
Consider why this distinction matters. If qada is always understood as creation, it would blur the line between God's decree and His commands, leading to theological errors.
This connects to broader debates on divine will and predestination.
5
Test your understanding
Answer the checkpoint question to confirm you can identify when qada is identical to the decreed thing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد يكون القضاء بمعنى الحكم والإلزام وهو مأخوذ من قولهم : «قضى القاضي على فلان بكذا» ، أي : حكم عليه به وحتمه . فنقول : إنه قضى المعاصي وقدرها على كل هذه الوجوه إلا على معنى أنه فرضها وأمر بها وحتم على العباد أن يفعلوها . فإن قال : فالقضاء عندكم هو المقضي أو غيره؟ . قيل له : هو على ضربين فالقضاء بمعنى الخلق هو المقضي ، لأن الخلق هو المخلوق والقضاء الذي هو الإلزام والإعلام والكتابة غير المقضيّ، لأن الأمر غير المأمور والخبر غير المخبر عنه إذا لم يكن خبراً عن نفسه أو عما يستحيل مفارقته له على بعض وجوه المفارقات المقتضية للغيرية . وكذلك الكتابة غير المكتوب .
And qada may be in the sense of judgment and obligation, and it is taken from their saying: 'The judge judged against so-and-so such-and-such,' i.e., he judged him with it and made it necessary. So we say: He decreed (qada) sins and predestined (qadar) them in all these senses except in the sense that He obligated them and commanded them and made them necessary for the servants to do them. Then if he says: Is qada in your view the decreed thing or something else? It is said to him: It is of two types: qada in the sense of creation is the decreed thing, because creation is the created thing; and qada which is obligation, notification, and writing is not the decreed thing, because the command is not the commanded thing, and the report is not the thing reported about unless it is a report about itself or about what is impossible to separate from it in some ways of separation that entail otherness. And similarly, writing is not the written thing.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is a definition and classification passage. Baqillani begins by identifying two meanings of the term qada (decree). First, qada can mean judgment and obligation, derived from the judge's verdict. Second, it can mean creation. He clarifies that when we say God decreed sins, we mean He created them and predestined them, not that He commanded them or made them obligatory. Then an objector asks whether qada is identical to the decreed thing (al-maqdi) or something else. Baqillani answers that it depends on the sense: qada in the sense of creation is identical to the created thing (the decreed thing), because the act of creating is the created object. However, qada in the sense of obligation, notification, or writing is distinct from its object, just as a command is not the same as the thing commanded, and a report is not the same as the thing reported about. An exception is when the report is about itself or about something inseparable from it, but generally otherness holds. So the identity or non-identity of qada with its object depends on which meaning is intended.

Key Terms
القضاء (al-qada, decree)
القدر (al-qadar, predestination)
الحكم (al-hukm, judgment)
الإلزام (al-ilzam, obligation)
الخلق (al-khalq, creation)
المقضي (al-maqdi, the decreed thing)
الأمر (al-amr, command)
الخبر (al-khabar, report)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think qada always means creation and thus is always identical to the decreed thing.
Correction: Baqillani shows that qada can also mean obligation, notification, or writing—in which case it is distinct from its object, just as a command is different from the thing commanded.

Checkpoint
In what sense is qada identical to the decreed thing, according to Baqillani?
A) In the sense of judgment
B) In the sense of creation
C) In the sense of obligation
D) In the sense of writing

Key Takeaway
The Arabic term qada can mean either creation (identical to the decreed thing) or obligation/notification (distinct from its object); the same word carries two senses.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that God decrees sins, do you ever feel despair or blame God for your own sins? How does Baqillani's distinction between creation and command change how you view your own responsibility for your actions? Will you now seek repentance more earnestly?
?
Are you quick to label God's decree as 'creation' when it suits you (e.g., when you succeed) but as 'command' when you want to avoid responsibility? Which meaning do you actually live by in your daily choices?
?
The lesson shows that the same Arabic word can carry two opposite implications. In your own life, are there beliefs or assumptions you hold that carry hidden double meanings? Are you willing to examine them as carefully as Baqillani examines qada, even if it means admitting error?
