Pleasure with God's Decree: General vs. Detailed
Baqillani responds to the objection about being pleased with God's decree by distinguishing general from detailed pleasure.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani distinguishes between being pleased with God's decree in general versus in detail, and why this distinction is crucial to avoid theological pitfalls.

Core Idea
We accept God's decree in general, but not every detail.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a challenging question: Are Muslims required to be pleased with everything God decrees, including sins and disbelief? He offers a nuanced answer that distinguishes between general and specific pleasure, using analogies from everyday Muslim speech to clarify his point.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and first answer
Read the Arabic passage from the beginning to the second answer. Notice how Baqillani first restricts pleasure to what God commands us to desire.
This is the first answer.
2
Identify the second answer and the key terms
Read the second answer where Baqillani introduces the distinction between الجملة (general) and التفصيل (detail). Note the term الإبهام (ambiguity).
3
Examine the analogies
Read the analogies about 'things belong to God' and 'creation perishes'. Understand how general statements can be true while detailed ones can be false or inappropriate.
This illustrates the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفترضون بقضاء الله وقدره ؟ . قيل لهم نرضى بقضاء الله الذي هو خلقه الذي أمرنا أن نريده ونرضاه. ولا نرضى من ذلك ما نهانا أن نرضى به، ولا نتقدّم بين يديه ولا نعترض على حكمه . وجواب آخر، وهو أننا نقول : إنا نرضى بقضاء الله في الجملة على كل حال . فإن قالوا : أفترضون الكفر والمعاصي التي هي من قضاء الله ؟ . قيل لهم : نحن نطلق الرضى بالقضاء في الجملة، ولا نطلقه في التفصيل لموضع الإبهام . كما يقول المسلمون كافة على الجملة : «الأشياء الله ، ولا يقولون على التفصيل : «الـولـد لله، والصــاحبـة والزوجة والشريك له . وكما نقول : «الخلق يفنون ويبيدون ويبطلون»، ولا نقول : «حجج الله تفنى وتبطل وتبيد» في نظائر هذا الذي يُطلق من وجه ويُمنع من وجه . ثم يقال لهم : أو ليس قد قضى الله تعالى موت النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم ، وعجز المسلمين والإقدار على غزوهم وهدم ثغورهم وسبي نسائهم ، وقضى إعانة الفراعنة والشياطين وسائر الكافرين وتعاونهم واستظهارهم على المسلمين فإن قالوا : أجل . قيل لهم : أفترضون بذلك أجمع ؟ . فإن قالوا : نعم . قيل لهم : مثله فيما سألوا عنه، وخرقوا الإجماع بركوب هذا الإطلاق . وإن قالوا : لا قيل لهم مثله فيما سألونا عنه
Then they said: Do you accept (be pleased with) God's decree and predestination? It is said to them: We accept God's decree which is His creation which He commanded us to desire and be pleased with. And we do not accept from that what He forbade us to be pleased with, and we do not outpace in between His hands nor object to His judgment. And another answer, which is that we say: We accept the decree of God in general in every case. Then they said: Do you accept disbelief and sins which are from God's decree? It is said to them: We apply the term 'pleasure' to the decree in general, but we do not apply it in detail due to ambiguity. Just as all Muslims say in general: 'Things belong to God,' but they do not say in detail: 'The child belongs to God, and the female companion, the wife, and the partner belong to Him.' And just as we say: 'Creation perishes, decays, and becomes null,' but we do not say: 'The proofs of God perish, become null, and decay' - in similar cases which are used in some respects and prevented in others. Then it is said to them: Has not God decreed the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family), and the inability of the Muslims and enabling [their enemies] to raid them, demolish their fortresses, capture their women, and decreed the assistance of the Pharaohs, devils, and all the disbelievers, their mutual assistance and support against the Muslims? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: Are you pleased with all of that? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: The same [applies] to what they asked about, and they have broken consensus by adopting this unqualified application. If they say: No. It is said to them: The same [applies] to what they asked us about.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer passage. Opponents ask whether Muslims are pleased with God's decree and predestination. Baqillani gives two answers. First, we are pleased with that part of God's decree which is His creation that He commanded us to desire and be pleased with, i.e., good things, and we are not pleased with what He forbade us to be pleased with (sins). Second, we say we are pleased with God's decree in general (الجملة) in all cases. Then a more specific objection: Are you pleased with disbelief and sins which are from God's decree? Baqillani responds that we use the term 'pleasure' (الرضا) in a general sense, but not in detail because of ambiguity. To illustrate, he provides analogies: Muslims say 'Things belong to God' in general, but they do not attribute specific improper things like 'a child belongs to God' (implying a physical offspring) in detail. Similarly, we say 'creation perishes' but do not say 'God's proofs perish' because that would be inappropriate. So some statements are allowed in general but not in detail. Then Baqillani turns the tables: He asks whether God decreed the death of the Prophet, the defeat of Muslims, the assistance of disbelievers, etc. If the opponents say they are pleased with all that, then they have broken consensus (because that would imply being pleased with evil). If they say they are not pleased, then they must also not be pleased with the disbelief and sins they asked about, thus conceding the point. This argument uses a reductio ad absurdum to show that one cannot be pleased with all details of God's decree, only in general.

Key Terms
الرضا (al-rida)
الجملة (al-jumla)
التفصيل (al-tafsil)
الإبهام (al-ibham)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that being pleased with God's decree means approving of every evil act individually.
Correction: Baqillani clarifies that pleasure is general, not detailed. We are pleased with God's overall decree but not with the specific evil acts in themselves.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, why do we not say 'we are pleased with disbelief' in detail?
A) Because disbelief is not from God's decree
B) Because of ambiguity (الإبهام)
C) Because we must always be pleased in detail
D) Because the Quran forbids it

Key Takeaway
We affirm pleasure with God's decree in general, but we do not apply that pleasure to specific evil acts in detail.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You say you are pleased with God's decree in general, but when a specific calamity strikes your life, do you truly accept it without complaint? What does your reaction reveal about your faith? Will you commit to surrendering that specific trial to God's wisdom?
?
The lesson says we do not accept disbelief and sins even though they are decreed. Are there sins you have allowed yourself to tolerate because you thought they were 'meant to be'? How will you actively reject them from now on?
?
Baqillani warns against attributing to God things that are inappropriate, like saying 'the child belongs to God.' Are there things you say about God that are actually improper? Examine your speech—do you ever blame God for your own mistakes? What will you change starting today?

The Reductio Argument: Consistency in Pleasure
Baqillani uses a reductio ad absurdum to force consistency on opponents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses a reductio ad absurdum to show that opponents must either accept being pleased with all calamities (breaking consensus) or deny being pleased with sins, thus conceding his point.

Core Idea
If you demand pleasure in detail, you must approve of all evil.

Baqillani now turns the tables on his opponents. He asks whether God decreed specific calamities like the death of the Prophet and the defeat of Muslims. If they say they are pleased with all that, they break consensus; if not, they contradict their own demand. This argument demonstrates the necessity of the general vs. detail distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read the reductio argument
Read from 'Then it is said to them' to the end. Notice the list of specific decrees: death of Prophet, Muslim defeats, etc.
2
Identify the two possible responses
The opponents must either say yes (they are pleased) or no. Baqillani shows the consequences of each.
3
Understand the conclusion
If they say yes, they break consensus. If no, they agree that pleasure in detail is not required, thus conceding Baqillani's point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Then they said: Do you accept (be pleased with) God's decree and predestination? It is said to them: We accept God's decree which is His creation which He commanded us to desire and be pleased with. And we do not accept from that what He forbade us to be pleased with, and we do not outpace in between His hands nor object to His judgment. And another answer, which is that we say: We accept the decree of God in general in every case. Then they said: Do you accept disbelief and sins which are from God's decree? It is said to them: We apply the term 'pleasure' to the decree in general, but we do not apply it in detail due to ambiguity. Just as all Muslims say in general: 'Things belong to God,' but they do not say in detail: 'The child belongs to God, and the female companion, the wife, and the partner belong to Him.' And just as we say: 'Creation perishes, decays, and becomes null,' but we do not say: 'The proofs of God perish, become null, and decay' - in similar cases which are used in some respects and prevented in others. Then it is said to them: Has not God decreed the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family), and the inability of the Muslims and enabling [their enemies] to raid them, demolish their fortresses, capture their women, and decreed the assistance of the Pharaohs, devils, and all the disbelievers, their mutual assistance and support against the Muslims? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: Are you pleased with all of that? If they say: Yes. It is said to them: The same [applies] to what they asked about, and they have broken consensus by adopting this unqualified application. If they say: No. It is said to them: The same [applies] to what they asked us about.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer passage. Opponents ask whether Muslims are pleased with God's decree and predestination. Baqillani gives two answers. First, we are pleased with that part of God's decree which is His creation that He commanded us to desire and be pleased with, i.e., good things, and we are not pleased with what He forbade us to be pleased with (sins). Second, we say we are pleased with God's decree in general (الجملة) in all cases. Then a more specific objection: Are you pleased with disbelief and sins which are from God's decree? Baqillani responds that we use the term 'pleasure' (الرضا) in a general sense, but not in detail because of ambiguity. To illustrate, he provides analogies: Muslims say 'Things belong to God' in general, but they do not attribute specific improper things like 'a child belongs to God' (implying a physical offspring) in detail. Similarly, we say 'creation perishes' but do not say 'God's proofs perish' because that would be inappropriate. So some statements are allowed in general but not in detail. Then Baqillani turns the tables: He asks whether God decreed the death of the Prophet, the defeat of Muslims, the assistance of disbelievers, etc. If the opponents say they are pleased with all that, then they have broken consensus (because that would imply being pleased with evil). If they say they are not pleased, then they must also not be pleased with the disbelief and sins they asked about, thus conceding the point. This argument uses a reductio ad absurdum to show that one cannot be pleased with all details of God's decree, only in general.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma', consensus)
الإطلاق (al-itlaq, unqualified application)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that being pleased with God's decree means approving of every specific evil act.
Correction: Baqillani shows that such approval would break consensus, so pleasure must be general.

Checkpoint
What does Baqillani argue would happen if opponents say they are pleased with all the specific calamities he lists?
A) They would be correct
B) They would break consensus
C) They would prove their point
D) They would be neutral

Key Takeaway
The reductio shows that detailed pleasure leads to absurdity; thus, pleasure must be understood in a general sense.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Can you identify a specific event in your life that you find difficult to accept as part of God's decree? How does Baqillani's distinction between general and detailed pleasure change your perspective on that event?
?
When you see oppression or suffering in the world, do you feel pressure to be pleased with it simply because it is decreed? How does this lesson free you from that burden while still affirming your trust in God's wisdom?
?
Are you willing to admit that there are aspects of God's decree that you are not pleased with in detail? If not, might you be falling into the very inconsistency Baqillani warns about? What would it look like to hold both general pleasure and honest displeasure with specific harms?

General vs. Specific Approval of Divine Decree
Baqillani refutes the objection that Muslims must be pleased with sins as God's decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Muslims affirm divine decree in general but do not approve of specific sins, and how Baqillani defends this position against an objection.

Core Idea
Approving God's decree does not mean approving every specific evil.

How can Muslims affirm that everything happens by God's decree without approving sins? This is a classic objection. Baqillani answers by drawing a crucial distinction: we approve the decree generally, but not in detail. He then turns the question back on the objector to show the absurdity of blanket approval. Read on to see how this argument unfolds.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial answer
Read the opening exchange. Notice the question and Baqillani's immediate distinction between general (jumla) and detailed (tafsil) approval.
Pay attention to the term 'ibham' (ambiguity) as the reason for not approving in detail.
2
Examine the analogies
Baqillani gives two analogies to clarify the distinction. Identify them and see how they illustrate the principle: some expressions are allowed generally but not in detail.
The first analogy is about saying 'things belong to God' but not applying that to specific partners. The second is about perishing but not applying to God's proofs.
3
Follow the counter-argument
Read the second part where Baqillani turns the tables. He lists specific painful decrees and asks whether the objector approves of them. This traps the opponent into either breaking consensus or conceding.
This is a typical kalam reductio ad absurdum.
4
Synthesize the lesson
Combine the two parts: the distinction and the reductio. Understand how together they form a complete defence of the Sunni position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : أفترضون الكفر والمعاصي التي هي من قضاء الله ؟ . قيل لهم : نحن نطلق الرضى بالقضاء في الجملة، ولا نطلقه في التفصيل لموضع الإبهام . كما يقول المسلمون كافة على الجملة : الأشياء لله ، ولا يقولون على التفصيل : الولد لله، والصاحبة والزوجة والشريك له . وكما نقول : الخلق يفنون ويبيدون ويبطلون، ولا نقول : حجج الله تفنى وتبطل وتبيد في نظائر هذا الذي يُطلق من وجه ويُمنع من وجه . ثم يقال لهم : أو ليس قد قضى الله تعالى موت النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم ، وعجز المسلمين والإقدار على غزوهم وهدم ثغورهم وسبي نسائهم ، وقضى إعانة الفراعنة والشياطين وسائر الكافرين وتعاونهم واستظهارهم على المسلمين فإن قالوا : أجل . قيل لهم : أفترضون بذلك أجمع ؟ . فإن قالوا : نعم . قيل لهم : مثله فيما سألوا عنه، وخرقوا الإجماع بركوب هذا الإطلاق . وإن قالوا : لا قيل لهم مثله فيما سألونا عنه
If they say: 'Do you approve of disbelief and sins which are from God's decree?' It is said to them: 'We apply approval of the decree in general, but we do not apply it in detail due to ambiguity. Just as all Muslims say in general: 'Things belong to God,' but they do not say in detail: 'The son belongs to God, nor the female companion, nor the wife, nor the partner for Him.' And just as we say: 'Creatures perish, become extinct, and become void,' but we do not say: 'The proofs of God perish, become void, and become extinct' in similar matters which are affirmed from one aspect and prevented from another.' Then it is said to them: 'Did God not decree the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him and his family), and the inability of the Muslims, and empowering [their enemies] to invade them, demolish their fortresses, and capture their women, and did He not decree assistance for the Pharaohs, devils, and all disbelievers, and their mutual help and dominance over the Muslims?' If they say: 'Yes.' It is said to them: 'Do you approve of all that?' If they say: 'Yes.' It is said to them: 'Then the same applies to what they asked about, and they have broken the consensus by employing this unrestricted application.' And if they say: 'No,' it is said to them: 'The same applies to what they asked us about.'
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer argument concerning approval of God's decree (al-rida bi al-qada). The objectors ask whether Muslims approve of disbelief and sins since they are decreed by God. Baqillani's answer has two parts. First, he makes a distinction: Muslims approve of the decree in general but not in detail, because affirming divine decree does not mean approving every specific evil act. He gives analogies: Muslims say 'all things belong to God' in general, but they do not say in detail that God has a son, spouse, or partner. Similarly, they say creatures perish, but they do not say God's proofs perish. So some expressions are permitted from one perspective and forbidden from another. Second, he turns the argument back on the questioner. He asks whether they approve of specific decrees such as the death of the Prophet, the suffering of Muslims, and the empowerment of disbelievers. If the questioner approves of all that, then they have broken consensus by applying approval without restriction; if they disapprove, then they have conceded the point against themselves. The structure is classic kalam argumentation: drawing a precise distinction then trapping the opponent in inconsistency. Baqillani thus defends the Sunni position that one must affirm divine decree without approving of evil deeds.

Key Terms
الرضى بالقضاء (al-rida bi al-qada)
الجملة (al-jumla)
التفصيل (al-tafsil)
الإبهام (al-ibham)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if Muslims affirm God's decree, they must approve of every specific sin or evil act.
Correction: Baqillani shows that approval is general, not detailed. One can affirm divine sovereignty while morally disapproving of sin.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, how do Muslims express approval of God's decree regarding sins?
A) They approve of it in general but not in detail.
B) They approve of it in detail also.
C) They do not approve of it at all.
D) They approve only of the decree of disbelievers.

Key Takeaway
Muslims affirm God's decree in general but do not approve of specific sins, and this distinction is defended by logical argument and analogy.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face a trial or setback in your life, do you find yourself falling into despair or resentment against God's decree? How does Baqillani's distinction between general approval and specific detail help you to submit to Allah's will while still feeling the pain of the moment? What one step will you take today to practice that distinction in your heart?
?
Do you ever catch yourself judging others' sins harshly, forgetting that they too are part of Allah's decree? How does this lesson force you to reconcile your disapproval of the sin with your acceptance of the decree? Will you choose to humble yourself and pray for the guidance of those you consider sinners?
?
The objectors in this passage tried to use divine decree to justify approval of evil. In your own life, have you ever used the argument 'it was written' to excuse your own negligence or sin? What would it take for you to stop using qadar as a shield and instead take full responsibility for your choices while still trusting in Allah's plan? Are you ready to make that change today?

Divine Decree

Allah Provides Both Halal and Haram
Baqillani asserts and proves that Allah provides both halal and haram.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah is the sole provider of all sustenance, whether lawful or unlawful, and the Qur'anic and rational proofs for this doctrine.

Core Idea
Allah's provision covers both halal and haram; nothing escapes His providence.

Imam Baqillani opens this passage with a direct question: do Muslims believe Allah provides both halal and haram? He answers with a firm 'yes' and marshals Qur'anic evidence and a compelling rational inference. This lesson lays the foundation for the Sunni understanding of divine provision (rizq) as encompassing all that sustains life, regardless of its legal status.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and note the question
Begin by reading the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the opening question: 'Do you say that Allah provides the lawful and the unlawful?'
This question sets the stage for the entire discussion.
2
Identify the Qur'anic proofs
Baqillani cites several verses. Find each one and see how they connect creation, provision, and death to establish Allah as the sole Provider.
The verse 'There is no creature but on Allah is its provision' is key.
3
Understand the logical inference
Consider the example of a person who eats only haram his whole life. If haram were not provision, Allah would have failed to provide for him. This proves that haram can be rizq.
This is a powerful rational argument.
4
Reflect on the poetic summary by Ibn Ruslan
Read the line: 'Provision is what benefits, even if unlawful.' This concisely captures the doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القول في الأرزاق فإن قالوا : أفتقولون إن الله يرزق الحلال والحرام ؟ . قيل لهم : أجل ، وقد دلّ على ذلك بقوله : الله الذي خلقكم ثم رزقكم ثم يميتكم ثم يحييكم . فلما كان منفرداً بالخلق والإماتة اعلم أن الله هو الرازق على الحقيقة ولا رازق على الحقيقة سواه ودليله قوله عزّ وجلّ من سورة القصص : كل شيء رزقاً من لدنا ، وقوله في سورة سبأ : الله وما أنفقتم من شيء فهو يخلفه وهو خير الرازقين وحسبنا أيضاً قوله : وما من دابة إلا على الله رزقها ، ففي هذه الآية إثبات أن الرزق قد يكون محرماً لأنه ثبت أن إيصال الرزق إلى كل حيوان واقع لعموم بحسب الوعد وبحسب الاستحقاق، ثم قد نرى إنساناً لا يأكل من الحلال طول عمره، فلو لم يكن الحرام رزقاً لكان الله تعالى ما أوصل رزقه إليه، فعلمنا أن الحرام قد يكون رزقاً وقال ابن رسلان في ألفية الزيد المشهورة. يرزق من يشاء ومن شاء احرما والرزق ما ينفع ولو محرما أي أنه يرزق من يشاء ما شاء من الرزق ومن شاء أحرمه ما شاء فيه . وفي رواية حرما وكلاهما بمعنى منع والألف فيها للإطلاق أو أنه تعالى يرزق من يشاء بأن يوسع عليه فيه ومن يشاء حرمه بأن يضيق عليه فيه لأنه تعالى هو الرازق فلا رازق غيره وكل يستوفي رزق نفسه ولا يتصور أن يأكل رزق غيره ولا أن يأكل غيره رزقه لأن ما قدره الله تعالى غذاء الشخص يجب أن يأكله أن يأكله غيره . ويمتنع الصدقات قال البغدادي في أصوله ص : ١٤٤، ١٤٥ ، وزعمت القدرية أن الله عزّ وجل لم يقسم الأرزاق إلا على الوجه الذي حكم به من استحقاق المواريث وما فرض من سهم لأهلها وما فرض من الغنائم لذوي القربى ومن ذكر معهم. وزعموا أن الإنسان قد يفوته ما رزقه الله عزّ وجلّ وأنه قد يأكل رزق غيره إذا غصب شيئاً وأكله وأجازوا أن يزيد الرزق بالطلب وينقص بالتواني. وقال أهل الحق إن كل من أكل شيئاً أو شرب فإنما تناول رزق نفسه حلالاً كان أو حراماً ولا يأكل أحد رزق غيره. ويجب على القدرية في قود أصلها أن يقولوا فيمن غصب جارية فأولدها بالحرام ولداً وسقى ذلك الولد ألباناً مغصوبة حتى نشأ، ثم ذلك من الحرام إلى أن بلغ وصار لصاً فلم يأكل ولم يشرب طول عمره إلا من الحرام ثم مات على ذلك، إن الله ما رزقه شيئاً. وكذلك الدابة من نتاج مغصوب إذا لم يأكله من غير الحرام لم يكن الله رازقاً لها عندهم. وهذا خلاف قول الله عزّ وجلّ: وما من دابة إلا على الله رزقها .
Chapter on Provisions. If they say: 'Do you say that Allah provides both the lawful and the unlawful?' It is said to them: 'Yes, and He has indicated that by His saying: “Allah is He Who created you, then provided for you, then will cause you to die, then will give you life.” Since He is unique in creation and causing death.' Know that Allah is the Provider in reality, and no provider in reality besides Him. Its proof is His word, Mighty and Majestic, from Surah Qasas: “Everything as provision from Us,” and His word in Surah Saba': “Allah, and whatever you spend in good, He will replace it, and He is the best of providers.” Sufficient for us also is His word: “And there is no moving creature but on Allah is its provision.” In this verse is proof that provision may be forbidden (haram), because it is established that the delivery of provision to every living creature is actualized universally according to promise and according to desert. Then we see a man who does not eat lawful food his entire lifetime; if the unlawful were not provision, then Allah would not have delivered his provision to him. Thus we know that the unlawful may be provision. And Ibn Ruslan said in his Alfiyya known as al-Zayd: “He provides whom He wills, and whom He wills He deprives. Provision is what benefits, even if unlawful.” Meaning that He provides whom He wills what He wills of provision, and whom He wills He deprives of what He wills. In another narration: “He deprives,” both meaning prohibition, and the alif is for absoluteness. Or that He, exalted, provides whom He wills by expanding it for him, and whom He wills He deprives by straitening it for him, because He is the Provider, so no provider other than Him. Everyone receives his own provision, and it is not conceivable that one eats another's provision, nor that another eats his provision, because what Allah has decreed as nourishment for a person must be eaten by him. And alms are prevented. Al-Baghdadi said in his Usul (p. 144-145): The Qadariyya claimed that Allah did not apportion provisions except in the manner He ruled concerning the entitlement of inheritances, the shares ordained for their recipients, and the shares of spoils for relatives and those mentioned with them. They claimed that a person may miss what Allah has provided him, and that he may eat another's provision if he usurps something and eats it, and they allowed that provision increases by seeking and decreases by negligence. The people of truth said: Everyone who eats something or drinks only consumes his own provision, lawful or unlawful, and no one eats another's provision. It is incumbent upon the Qadariyya, according to the foundation of their principle, that regarding one who usurps a female slave, procreates with her unlawfully a child, feeds that child with usurped milk until he grows up, then he is from the unlawful until he reaches adulthood and becomes a thief, and he does not eat or drink throughout his life except from the unlawful, then he dies in that state — they must say that Allah did not provide him anything. Similarly, an animal from a usurped offspring if it does not eat anything except from the unlawful, then Allah is not its provider according to them. This contradicts the saying of Allah: “And there is no moving creature but on Allah is its provision.”
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof concerning divine provision (rizq), establishing that Allah provides both halal and haram, and refuting the Qadariyya who limit provision to lawful means. Baqillani begins with the question: do you say Allah provides both? He answers yes, citing Quranic verses that link creation and provision. He then states the principle: Allah is the only true provider. The proof includes verses from Surah Qasas, Surah Saba', and Surah Hud. The key inference: if a person eats only haram his whole life, and haram were not provision, then Allah would not have provided him, which is absurd; therefore haram can be provision. He quotes Ibn Ruslan's line: 'Provision is what benefits, even if unlawful.' Next, he quotes al-Baghdadi to present and refute the Qadariyya position. The Qadariyya claimed provision is only through lawful means like inheritance and spoils, and that a person can miss his provision or eat another's. Baqillani, through al-Baghdadi, affirms the Sunni position that everyone eats his own provision whether halal or haram, and it is impossible to eat another's. He illustrates with a thought experiment: a person who lives only on usurped goods his whole life — if haram is not provision, then Allah never provided him, which contradicts the verse that every creature's provision is from Allah. Thus the correct view is that provision includes both lawful and unlawful, and Allah is the sole provider.

Key Terms
الرزق (al-rizq)
الحرام (al-haram)
الحلال (al-halal)
الرازق (al-razzaq)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Allah only provides lawful sustenance.
Correction: Allah provides both lawful and unlawful, as proven by the man who eats only haram his whole life; otherwise Allah would have failed to provide for him.

Checkpoint
According to Baqillani, what is the evidence that haram can be a form of rizq?
A) The verse 'Allah is the best of providers' explicitly says so.
B) Because we see a person who eats only haram his whole life, and if it were not rizq, Allah would not have provided him.
C) Because the Qadariyya said so.
D) Because the Prophet said so in a hadith.

Key Takeaway
Allah alone is the true Provider, and His provision includes both the lawful and the unlawful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every morsel you eat—whether from a halal or haram source—is from Allah? If so, how does that change your attitude towards earning and consuming?
?
Reflect on a time you earned or consumed something of doubtful permissibility. Did you consider that it was still Allah's provision? Does that comfort or disturb you? What does this lesson demand of you now?
?
If Allah provides both halal and haram, then why do you strive for halal? What separates the believer from the negligent in this regard? How will you act on this distinction starting today?

Divine Decree

Refuting the Qadariyya on Provision
Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya claim that provision is only lawful and can be missed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qadariyya position on provision and how Sunni scholars refute it using rational and scriptural arguments.

Core Idea
Everyone eats only their own provision, whether halal or haram, as decreed by Allah.

This lesson continues Baqillani's treatment of divine provision by presenting and dismantling the Qadariyya claim that provision is limited to lawful means and can be missed or usurped. Through a striking thought experiment, Baqillani demonstrates the logical necessity that all sustenance, even if unlawfully obtained, is ultimately from Allah.

Guided Path
1
Read the Qadariyya claim
Read the passage describing the Qadariyya view: they believed provision is only through lawful means like inheritance and spoils, and that a person can miss his provision or eat another's.
2
Understand the Sunni counter-statement
Notice the Sunni response: everyone consumes only his own provision, lawful or unlawful, and no one can eat another's. This is the correct view.
3
Analyze the thought experiment
Consider the example of a usurper who lives only on stolen goods and his child raised on usurped milk. If these are not provision from Allah, then Allah never provided for them, contradicting 'There is no creature but on Allah is its provision'.
This thought experiment exposes the absurdity of the Qadariyya position.

باب القول في الأرزاق فإن قالوا : أفتقولون إن الله يرزق الحلال والحرام ؟ . قيل لهم : أجل ، وقد دلّ على ذلك بقوله : الله الذي خلقكم ثم رزقكم ثم يميتكم ثم يحييكم . فلما كان منفرداً بالخلق والإماتة اعلم أن الله هو الرازق على الحقيقة ولا رازق على الحقيقة سواه ودليله قوله عزّ وجلّ من سورة القصص : كل شيء رزقاً من لدنا ، وقوله في سورة سبأ : الله وما أنفقتم من شيء فهو يخلفه وهو خير الرازقين وحسبنا أيضاً قوله : وما من دابة إلا على الله رزقها ، ففي هذه الآية إثبات أن الرزق قد يكون محرماً لأنه ثبت أن إيصال الرزق إلى كل حيوان واقع لعموم بحسب الوعد وبحسب الاستحقاق، ثم قد نرى إنساناً لا يأكل من الحلال طول عمره، فلو لم يكن الحرام رزقاً لكان الله تعالى ما أوصل رزقه إليه، فعلمنا أن الحرام قد يكون رزقاً وقال ابن رسلان في ألفية الزيد المشهورة. يرزق من يشاء ومن شاء احرما والرزق ما ينفع ولو محرما أي أنه يرزق من يشاء ما شاء من الرزق ومن شاء أحرمه ما شاء فيه . وفي رواية حرما وكلاهما بمعنى منع والألف فيها للإطلاق أو أنه تعالى يرزق من يشاء بأن يوسع عليه فيه ومن يشاء حرمه بأن يضيق عليه فيه لأنه تعالى هو الرازق فلا رازق غيره وكل يستوفي رزق نفسه ولا يتصور أن يأكل رزق غيره ولا أن يأكل غيره رزقه لأن ما قدره الله تعالى غذاء الشخص يجب أن يأكله أن يأكله غيره . ويمتنع الصدقات قال البغدادي في أصوله ص : ١٤٤، ١٤٥ ، وزعمت القدرية أن الله عزّ وجل لم يقسم الأرزاق إلا على الوجه الذي حكم به من استحقاق المواريث وما فرض من سهم لأهلها وما فرض من الغنائم لذوي القربى ومن ذكر معهم. وزعموا أن الإنسان قد يفوته ما رزقه الله عزّ وجلّ وأنه قد يأكل رزق غيره إذا غصب شيئاً وأكله وأجازوا أن يزيد الرزق بالطلب وينقص بالتواني. وقال أهل الحق إن كل من أكل شيئاً أو شرب فإنما تناول رزق نفسه حلالاً كان أو حراماً ولا يأكل أحد رزق غيره. ويجب على القدرية في قود أصلها أن يقولوا فيمن غصب جارية فأولدها بالحرام ولداً وسقى ذلك الولد ألباناً مغصوبة حتى نشأ، ثم ذلك من الحرام إلى أن بلغ وصار لصاً فلم يأكل ولم يشرب طول عمره إلا من الحرام ثم مات على ذلك، إن الله ما رزقه شيئاً. وكذلك الدابة من نتاج مغصوب إذا لم يأكله من غير الحرام لم يكن الله رازقاً لها عندهم. وهذا خلاف قول الله عزّ وجلّ: وما من دابة إلا على الله رزقها .
Chapter on Provisions. If they say: 'Do you say that Allah provides both the lawful and the unlawful?' It is said to them: 'Yes, and He has indicated that by His saying: “Allah is He Who created you, then provided for you, then will cause you to die, then will give you life.” Since He is unique in creation and causing death.' Know that Allah is the Provider in reality, and no provider in reality besides Him. Its proof is His word, Mighty and Majestic, from Surah Qasas: “Everything as provision from Us,” and His word in Surah Saba': “Allah, and whatever you spend in good, He will replace it, and He is the best of providers.” Sufficient for us also is His word: “And there is no moving creature but on Allah is its provision.” In this verse is proof that provision may be forbidden (haram), because it is established that the delivery of provision to every living creature is actualized universally according to promise and according to desert. Then we see a man who does not eat lawful food his entire lifetime; if the unlawful were not provision, then Allah would not have delivered his provision to him. Thus we know that the unlawful may be provision. And Ibn Ruslan said in his Alfiyya known as al-Zayd: “He provides whom He wills, and whom He wills He deprives. Provision is what benefits, even if unlawful.” Meaning that He provides whom He wills what He wills of provision, and whom He wills He deprives of what He wills. In another narration: “He deprives,” both meaning prohibition, and the alif is for absoluteness. Or that He, exalted, provides whom He wills by expanding it for him, and whom He wills He deprives by straitening it for him, because He is the Provider, so no provider other than Him. Everyone receives his own provision, and it is not conceivable that one eats another's provision, nor that another eats his provision, because what Allah has decreed as nourishment for a person must be eaten by him. And alms are prevented. Al-Baghdadi said in his Usul (p. 144-145): The Qadariyya claimed that Allah did not apportion provisions except in the manner He ruled concerning the entitlement of inheritances, the shares ordained for their recipients, and the shares of spoils for relatives and those mentioned with them. They claimed that a person may miss what Allah has provided him, and that he may eat another's provision if he usurps something and eats it, and they allowed that provision increases by seeking and decreases by negligence. The people of truth said: Everyone who eats something or drinks only consumes his own provision, lawful or unlawful, and no one eats another's provision. It is incumbent upon the Qadariyya, according to the foundation of their principle, that regarding one who usurps a female slave, procreates with her unlawfully a child, feeds that child with usurped milk until he grows up, then he is from the unlawful until he reaches adulthood and becomes a thief, and he does not eat or drink throughout his life except from the unlawful, then he dies in that state — they must say that Allah did not provide him anything. Similarly, an animal from a usurped offspring if it does not eat anything except from the unlawful, then Allah is not its provider according to them. This contradicts the saying of Allah: “And there is no moving creature but on Allah is its provision.”
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof concerning divine provision (rizq), establishing that Allah provides both halal and haram, and refuting the Qadariyya who limit provision to lawful means. Baqillani begins with the question: do you say Allah provides both? He answers yes, citing Quranic verses that link creation and provision. He then states the principle: Allah is the only true provider. The proof includes verses from Surah Qasas, Surah Saba', and Surah Hud. The key inference: if a person eats only haram his whole life, and haram were not provision, then Allah would not have provided him, which is absurd; therefore haram can be provision. He quotes Ibn Ruslan's line: 'Provision is what benefits, even if unlawful.' Next, he quotes al-Baghdadi to present and refute the Qadariyya position. The Qadariyya claimed provision is only through lawful means like inheritance and spoils, and that a person can miss his provision or eat another's. Baqillani, through al-Baghdadi, affirms the Sunni position that everyone eats his own provision whether halal or haram, and it is impossible to eat another's. He illustrates with a thought experiment: a person who lives only on usurped goods his whole life — if haram is not provision, then Allah never provided him, which contradicts the verse that every creature's provision is from Allah. Thus the correct view is that provision includes both lawful and unlawful, and Allah is the sole provider.

Key Terms
القدرية (al-Qadariyya)
الرزق (al-rizq)
الحرام (al-haram)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Provision is only that which is lawfully obtained; unlawful gain is not from Allah's provision.
Correction: Allah provides all sustenance, whether lawful or unlawful, as proven by the Qur'an and the absurdity of the Qadariyya stance.

Checkpoint
What did the Qadariyya claim about provision?
A) Allah provides only through lawful means and a person can eat another's provision.
B) Provision is only for believers.
C) Allah does not provide for those who sin.
D) Provision is fixed and cannot change.

Key Takeaway
Allah provides every creature with its sustenance; no one can eat another's provision, and the unlawfulness of the means does not negate it being from Allah.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you worry about your livelihood, are you not, in that moment, falling into the very doubt this passage condemns? What would it take for you to truly believe that your provision is guaranteed by Allah alone?
?
If all that you consume, even what you obtain through sin, is still from Allah's decree, how does that change the way you view your past sins? Will you repent and still trust that Allah's provision never fails?
?
The Qadariyya thought they could miss their provision if they didn't strive. Where in your life do you rely more on your own effort than on Allah's guarantee? What step can you take today to shift that trust?

Haram Can Be Rizq: The True Provider
Baqillani argues that haram can be rizq using Quran and logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that divine provision (rizq) is what one actually receives and benefits from, regardless of its legal status, and that haram can be considered rizq.

Core Idea
Provision is what reaches you, even if it is prohibited.

Imam al-Baqillani tackles a common theological puzzle: if Allah promises provision for every creature, how can someone live a lifetime consuming only what is forbidden? In this passage, he uses clear reasoning and Quranic support to show that provision is not defined by legality but by what one actually receives and benefits from. The lesson draws on Quranic verses and a poetic summary by Ibn Ruslan.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis, then read the literal translation to get a feel for Baqillani's argument.
Notice the Quranic verses cited.
2
Identify the key proofs
Find the Quranic proofs (al-Qasas and Saba) and the logical argument from observation of a person who eats only haram.
3
Understand the argument
Reflect on the empirical observation: if haram were not rizq, then a haram-only eater would lack provision from Allah, contradicting the Qur'an. Therefore, haram can be rizq.
This is the core reasoning.
4
Reflect on the poetic summary
Read Ibn Ruslan's verse and its explanation. Consider how it reinforces the definition of rizq as what benefits, not necessarily what is lawful.

اعلم أن الله هو الرازق على الحقيقة ولا رازق على الحقيقة سواه ودليله قوله عزّ وجلّ من سورة القصص : كل شيء رزقاً من لدنا ، وقوله في سورة سبأ : الله وما أنفقتم من شيء فهو يخلفه وهو خير الرازقين وحسبنا أيضاً قوله : ( وما من دابة إلا على الله رزقها ، ففي هذه الآية إثبات أن الرزق قد يكون محرماً لأنه ثبت أن إيصال الرزق إلى كل حيوان واقع لعموم بحسب الوعد وبحسب الاستحقاق، ثم قد نرى إنساناً لا يأكل من الحلال طول عمره، فلو لم يكن الحرام رزقاً لكان الله تعالى ما أوصل رزقه إليه، فعلمنا أن الحرام قد يكون رزقاً وقال ابن رسلان في ألفية الزيد المشهورة. يرزق من يشاء ومن شاء احرما والرزق ما ينفع ولو محرما أي أنه يرزق من يشاء ما شاء من الرزق ومن شاء أحرمه ما شاء فيه . وفي رواية حرما وكلاهما بمعنى منع والألف فيها للإطلاق أو أنه تعالى يرزق من يشاء بأن يوسع عليه فيه ومن يشاء حرمه بأن يضيق عليه فيه لأنه تعالى هو الرازق فلا رازق غيره وكل يستوفي رزق نفسه ولا يتصور أن يأكل رزق غيره ولا أن يأكل غيره رزقه لأن ما قدره الله تعالى غذاء الشخص يجب أن يأكله أن يأكله غيره .
Know that Allah is the true provider and there is no true provider besides Him. His proof is His saying in Surah al-Qasas: 'Everything as a provision from Us,' and His saying in Surah Saba: 'Allah - and whatever you spend He will replace it, and He is the best of providers.' Sufficient for us is also His saying: 'And there is no creature but upon Allah is its provision.' So in this verse is proof that provision may be prohibited, because it is established that the delivery of provision to every animal occurs universally according to promise and according to merit. Then we often see a person who eats nothing but haram throughout his life; if haram were not provision, then Allah would not have delivered his provision to him. So we know that haram may be provision. And Ibn Ruslan said in his famous Alfiyyah: 'He provides whom He wills, and whom He wills He deprives; provision is what benefits even if prohibited.' Meaning He provides whom He wills whatever provision He wills, and whom He wills He deprives of what He wills. In another narration 'harrama' (prohibited), both meaning prevention, and the alif is for release, or that He provides whom He wills by expanding it for him, and whom He wills He deprives by narrowing it for him, because He is the Provider and no provider other than Him. Everyone receives his own provision, and it is inconceivable that one eats another's provision or that another eats his provision, because what Allah has decreed as the food of a person must be eaten by him, not by another.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is an explanatory commentary on the nature of divine provision. It begins by asserting that Allah is the only true provider, supported by Quranic verses (al-Qasas and Saba). The key argument is that if haram were not rizq, then a person who consumes only haram his whole life would have no provision from Allah, which contradicts the Quranic promise that every creature has its provision from Allah. Therefore, haram can be rizq. The passage then quotes Ibn Ruslan's poetic summary: 'Provision is what benefits even if prohibited.' The explanation emphasizes that each individual consumes only their own decreed provision, not another's.

Refutation of Qadariyya on Provisions
Baqillani transmits al-Baghdadi's refutation of Qadariyya denial of haram as rizq.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani (via al-Baghdadi) refutes the Qadariyya claim that Allah's provision is limited to lawful means and that humans can miss or usurp provision, using a logical argument that forces a contradiction with the Quran.

Core Idea
Allah provides every creature, even through means we deem unlawful.

This passage is a powerful refutation of the Qadariyya sect, who argued that Allah's provision is confined to lawful channels like inheritance and spoils. Imam Baqillani transmits al-Baghdadi's argument showing that this view leads to the absurd conclusion that a person living entirely on haram receives no provision from Allah—contradicting the clear Quranic verse. Let's explore the argument step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that al-Baghdadi first states the Qadariyya view, then the response of Ahl al-Haqq, then a logical consequence.
2
Identify the two opposing views
The passage presents two views: the Qadariyya claim and the Ahl al-Haqq response. List the key points of each.
Qadariyya: provision only through lawful means; people can miss their provision. Ahl al-Haqq: everyone consumes their own provision, halal or haram.
3
Understand the reductio ad absurdum
Al-Baghdadi forces the Qadariyya into a logical extreme: a person who lives entirely on haram. According to their principle, such a person has no provision from Allah. That contradicts the Quranic verse about every creature's provision.
The reductio shows that the Qadariyya view leads to a denial of Allah's comprehensive providence.
4
Reflect on the Quranic evidence
The passage ends with the verse: 'And there is no creature but upon Allah is its provision.' Consider how this verse directly refutes the Qadariyya position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال البغدادي في أصوله ص : ١٤٤، ١٤٥ ، وزعمت القدرية أن الله عزّ وجل لم يقسم الأرزاق إلا على الوجه الذي حكم به من استحقاق المواريث وما فرض من سهم لأهلها وما فرض من الغنائم لذوي القربى ومن ذكر معهم. وزعموا أن الإنسان قد يفوته ما رزقه الله عزّ وجلّ وأنه قد يأكل رزق غيره إذا غصب شيئاً وأكله وأجازوا أن يزيد الرزق بالطلب وينقص بالتواني. وقال أهل الحق إن كل من أكل شيئاً أو شرب فإنما تناول رزق نفسه حلالاً كان أو حراماً ولا يأكل أحد رزق غيره. ويجب على القدرية في قود أصلها أن يقولوا فيمن غصب جارية فأولدها بالحرام ولداً وسقى ذلك الولد ألباناً مغصوبة حتى نشأ، ثم ذلك من الحرام إلى أن بلغ وصار لصاً فلم يأكل ولم يشرب طول عمره إلا من الحرام ثم مات على ذلك، إن الله ما رزقه شيئاً. وكذلك الدابة من نتاج مغصوب إذا لم يأكله من غير الحرام لم يكن الله رازقاً لها عندهم. وهذا خلاف قول الله عزّ وجل: ( وما من دابة إلا على الله رزقها )
Al-Baghdadi said in his Usool (pp. 144-145): The Qadariyya claimed that Allah did not divide provisions except according to the ruling by entitlement of inheritance, what was prescribed of shares for its people, what was prescribed of spoils for kin and those mentioned with them. They claimed that a person may miss what Allah provided him, and that he may eat another's provision if he usurps something and eats it, and they allowed that provision increases by seeking and decreases by laziness. The people of truth said: Every person who eats or drinks takes only his own provision, halal or haram, and no one eats another's provision. The Qadariyya, according to the logical consequence of their principle, must say concerning one who usurps a slave-girl, produces offspring with her unlawfully, and feeds that offspring with usurped milk until he grows, then continues on that haram until he becomes a thief and never eats or drinks his whole life except from haram, then dies in that state: 'Allah did not provide him anything.' Similarly, the animal from usurped offspring, if it eats nothing but haram, is not provided by Allah according to them. This contradicts Allah's saying: 'And there is no creature but upon Allah is its provision.'
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a quotation from al-Baghdadi providing a polemical refutation of the Qadariyya position on provisions. It first states the Qadariyya view: they restrict Allah's provision to lawful means (inheritance, prescribed shares) and allow that people can miss their provision or eat another's provision through usurpation. Ahl al-Haqq (the people of truth) respond that everyone consumes only their own provision, lawful or not. Then al-Baghdadi forces a logical consequence on the Qadariyya: in the extreme case of a person who lives entirely on haram (from usurped milk to theft), they would have to say Allah provided nothing to that person. The same applies to an animal from usurped stock. This contradicts the clear Quranic assertion that every creature's provision is upon Allah.

أهل الحق
الرزق
الغصب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Qadariyya deny divine involvement in all sustenance, but actually they restrict provision to lawful means.
Correction: The passage shows that the Qadariyya do not deny Allah's provision entirely; they limit it to lawful channels, which leads to the absurd result that a person who eats only haram has no provision from Allah.

A) He is still provided by Allah because he owns the goods

C) He is provided by Allah in some hidden way
D) He is not provided by Allah because he stole

Key Takeaway
Allah's provision encompasses all sustenance, whether halal or haram, and no creature is left unprovided, refuting the Qadariyya restriction of rizq to lawful means.

Allah Provides Both Halal and Haram
Baqillani affirms Allah's provision of both halal and haram with a Quranic proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani asserts that Allah provides both halal and haram, and how he proves it from the Quran.

Core Idea
Allah alone provides all sustenance, whether lawful or unlawful.

In this passage, Baqillani addresses a key question about divine providence: does Allah provide both halal and haram? The objectors might think that haram sustenance is not from Allah, but Baqillani affirms it and gives a clear Quranic proof. As you read, notice how he links creation, provision, death, and life to establish Allah’s exclusive control over all provisions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the overall argument.
Notice the concise dialectical style.
2
Identify the key elements
Identify the objection, the answer, the Quranic verse, and the logical conclusion. See how each part builds on the previous.
3
Reflect on the significance
Why does this refute the idea that haram is not from Allah? How does the verse's sequence prove the point?
This connects to the broader doctrine of qadar (divine decree).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القول في الأرزاق
فإن قالوا : أفتقولون إن الله يرزق الحلال والحرام ؟
قيل لهم : أجل، وقد دلّ على ذلك بقوله : الله الذي خلقكم ثم رزقكم ثم يميتكم ثم يحييكم (سورة الروم : ٤٠) . فلما كان منفرداً بالخلق والإماتة والإحياء، كان منفرداً بتولّي الأرزاق.
Chapter on the statement about provisions. If they say: Do you say that Allah provides the halal and the haram? It is said to them: Yes, and that is indicated by His saying: 'Allah is the One who created you, then provided for you, then causes you to die, then gives you life' (Surah ar-Rum: 40). So when He is unique in creation, causing death, and giving life, He is unique in undertaking the provisions.
Source pages p. 374

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical definition and proof. It opens with the chapter heading 'Statement on provisions'. Then an objection is posed: 'Do you say that Allah provides both halal and haram?' The answer is affirmative, and a Quranic proof is given: the verse from Surah ar-Rum (40) which links creation, provision, death, and resurrection. The logical conclusion is that just as Allah alone creates, causes death, and resurrects, so He alone undertakes all provisions. This establishes that all sustenance, whether halal or haram, comes from Allah.

الحلال
الحرام
الخلق
الإماتة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That haram sustenance is not from Allah because it is forbidden.
Correction: The verse shows all provision is from Allah regardless of its legal status; the haram status is about permissibility, not source.

Checkpoint
On what basis does Baqillani argue that Allah provides both halal and haram?
A) By rational necessity
B) By the verse of Surah ar-Rum that links creation, provision, death, and life
C) By consensus of the scholars
D) By the argument that haram cannot exist without a provider

Key Takeaway
Allah alone provides all forms of sustenance, whether halal or haram, as proven by His exclusive control over creation, life, and death.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
You have read that Allah alone provides, just as He alone creates and gives life. When you face financial anxiety or scarcity, who do you truly rely on? Honestly, does your heart depend on your job, savings, or other people more than on Allah? What will you change in your daily thoughts to make Allah your sole provider?
?
If you have ever blamed others for your lack of provision or felt envious of someone else’s wealth, this lesson refutes that. Are you willing to repent from such blame and envy? Write down one specific way you will cultivate contentment with what Allah has given you, starting today.

How Allah Provides Haram: Nourishment, Not Ownership
Baqillani answers an objection by distinguishing two meanings of provision.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between Allah providing haram as physical sustenance versus as lawful ownership, and why this matters for the doctrine of divine providence.

Core Idea
Allah provides haram as nourishment, not as lawful permission.

Imam al-Baqillani addresses a key objection regarding divine providence: how can it be said that Allah provides what is forbidden? In this passage, he clarifies that 'providing' does not always mean making something lawful or permissible. Instead, it can refer to physical sustenance, while the permission to consume is reserved for halal. This distinction resolves an apparent contradiction and aligns with Muslim consensus.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and answer
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice the structure: a question is posed, then answered.
2
Identify the two meanings of provision
Baqillani distinguishes two senses: (1) nourishment/sustenance and (2) ownership/permission. Halal is provided in both senses; haram only in the first.
The key Arabic terms are 'ghidha' (nourishment) and 'qiwam' (sustenance) versus 'tamlik' (ownership) and 'ibaha' (permissibility).
3
Connect to consensus
Baqillani appeals to the consensus of Muslims that haram is not permissible to consume. This shows his answer is not novel but rooted in agreed doctrine.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا : فما معنى قولكم إنه يرزق الحرام؟ . قيل لهم: تأويل ذلك أن يجعله غذاء للأبدان وقواماً للأجسام، لا على معنى التمليك والإباحة لتناوله، لأن ذلك مما قد أجمع المسلمون على خلافه . وهو تعالى رازق الحلال على الوجهين جميعاً.
If they say: What is the meaning of your statement that He provides the haram? It is said to them: The interpretation of that is that He makes it nourishment for bodies and sustenance for physical constitutions, not in the sense of ownership and permissibility of consumption, because that is something which the Muslims have agreed upon. And He provides the halal in both senses.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer. The objector asks how Allah can be said to provide haram. The answer clarifies that 'providing' here means making it a means of physical nourishment and sustenance for the body, not that Allah makes it lawful property or permits its consumption. The latter is reserved for halal. The answer relies on Muslim consensus that haram is not permissible to consume lawfully, yet it is still provision in terms of sustaining life. Halal is provided in both senses: as nourishment and as rightful ownership.

Key Terms

الرزق
التمليك
الإباحة
الغذاء
القوام

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction

Correction: The passage clarifies that 'providing' can mean merely sustaining life, not giving lawful permission.

Checkpoint

A) Allah makes it lawful to consume
B) Allah makes it a physical nourishment, not lawful property
C) Allah only provides halal, but people mistakenly take haram
D) Allah provides haram only to disbelievers

Key Takeaway
Allah provides the halal in both senses (nourishment and lawful ownership) but provides the haram only in the sense of sustaining physical life, not as permissible property.

Refuting the Definition of Rizq as Ownership
Baqillani refutes the equation of rizq with ownership using consensus on infants and animals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani rejects the equation of rizq with ownership (tamlik) using the consensus on infants and animals and a logical argument about haram.

Core Idea
Rizq is not ownership; infants and animals are provided without owning.

Baqillani continues his refutation of alternative definitions of rizq. Here, he confronts the proposal that rizq simply means ownership (tamlik). He offers two decisive arguments: first, the consensus of Muslims that infants and animals are provided despite not owning what they consume; second, a logical reductio that would make even haram a form of provision if ownership is equated with mere ability.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice how Baqillani presents the opponent's view and then his refutation.
Pay attention to the key terms: التمليك, الملك, الرزق.
2
Identify the opponent's claim
The opponent suggests that rizq should be understood as tamlik (ownership). Locate this in the Arabic.
3
Understand the first refutation: consensus
Baqillani appeals to ijma': everyone agrees that infants and animals are provided even though they do not own the milk or grass. Why does this disprove the definition?
It shows rizq is broader than ownership.
4
Understand the second refutation: absurd consequence
If ownership is redefined as mere ability (qudra), then even haram would be 'owned' by the one able to consume it, making Allah a provider of haram. Why is this problematic?
This exposes the logical flaw in the redefinition.
5
Synthesize the lesson
Explain in your own words why Baqillani's refutation is convincing. What does it teach us about the nature of rizq?
Rizq is about actual provision from Allah, not legal ownership.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا ما أنكرتم أن يكون معنى الرزق هو معنى التمليك ؟ . قيل لهم: أنكرنا ذلك لإجماع الأمة على أن الطفل مرزوق لما يرضعه من ثدي أمه؛ وعلى أن البهائم من ولد النعم مرزوقة لما تغتذي به كلها مرزوقة لما ترتعيه من حشائش من لبنها، وكذلك هي الأرض ونباتها؛ وأن البهيمة والطفل لا يملكان ذلك كونه رزقاً لهما مع لأنهم متفقون على أن لبن سائر النعم ملك لربها دون سخالها. فبطل ما سألتم عنه. وعلى أنه لو كان الرزق هو التمليك والملك عندهم بمعنى القدرة، لكان الباري مملكاً للحرام من حيث كان مقدراً على تناوله وعلى أن يكون رازقاً له بهذا المعنى . ولا مهرب لهم من ذلك
If they say: What prevents you from understanding the meaning of provision as ownership? It is said to them: We reject that due to the consensus of the ummah that the infant is provided with what he sucks from his mother's breast; and that the young of livestock are provided with what they feed on, all of them are provided with what they graze from plants and their milk; similarly, the earth and its plants; and that the animal and infant do not own that, yet it is provision for them, because they agree that the milk of all livestock is the property of their owner, not of their offspring. Therefore your question is invalid. And if provision were ownership and possession in the sense of ability (power), then the Creator would be making the haram owned by the one who has the ability to consume it, and would be a provider in that sense. And they have no escape from this.
Source pages p. 375

Commentary
This passage is a second objection-and-answer. The objector suggests defining rizq as tamlik (ownership). Baqillani refutes this by appealing to consensus (ijma): everyone agrees that a nursing infant and grazing animals are provided for (marzuq) even though they do not own the milk or grass they consume. The milk belongs to the owner of the animal, not to the offspring. Similarly, plants belong to the landowner. Yet these are clearly provisions from Allah for the creatures. This shows tamlik cannot be the definition. Then a further argument is made: if one redefines 'ownership' as mere ability (qudra) to consume, then even haram would be owned by the consumer in that sense, which the objector likely denies. Thus the definition fails.

الملك
الرزق
الإجماع
الطفل
البهائم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Rizq requires legal ownership.
Correction: Rizq is broader: infants and animals are provided without owning, so provision is from Allah regardless of ownership.

Checkpoint
What evidence does Baqillani use to disprove that rizq means ownership?
A) The Quranic verse that Allah provides for all creatures
B) The consensus that infants and animals are provided even though they do not own what they consume
C) The argument that ownership requires legal capacity
D) The impossibility of owning haram

Key Takeaway
Rizq is not defined by ownership; consensus on infants and animals proves that provision from Allah extends beyond legal possession.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly trust that Allah provides for you even when you have no ownership or control over your circumstances, like the infant who depends entirely on its mother? Or do you feel anxious only when you possess something tangible?

Does the Killed Person Die at His Appointed Term?
Baqillani opens the chapter on lifetimes with a question.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the initial framing of the kalam debate on whether a killed person dies at his predetermined term or has it cut short.

Core Idea
The killing and the term are both from God's decree.

Imam Baqillani begins a new chapter on the topic of appointed terms (al-ajal) by posing a classic theological question. When a person is killed, does he die at the exact moment God had decreed for his natural death, or does the killing interrupt and shorten that term? This question sets the stage for exploring how divine predestination relates to secondary causes like human violence.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening question
Read the Arabic text and its translation carefully. Notice that it is a direct question posed by an imagined interlocutor. This style is common in kalam works to introduce a problem.
The phrase 'فإن قال قائل' signals a hypothetical objection or inquiry.
2
Understand the two alternatives
Identify the two possibilities: either the killed person dies at his appointed term (أجله المحكوم له به) or his term is cut short (مقطوع عليه أجله). Reflect on the implications of each for divine decree and human responsibility.
3
Connect to broader kalam debates
Consider why this question matters in Islamic theology. It touches on predestination, justice, and the relationship between God's decree and secondary causes. This lesson is the entry point for a longer discussion.
The commentary mentions that the question presupposes a fixed term for everyone.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب القول في الآجال

فإن قال قائل: فخبرونا عن المقتول أيموت بأجله المحكوم له به، أم هو مقطوع عليه أجله؟
Chapter on the Appointed Terms. For if someone says: Inform us about the killed person: does he die at his appointed term decreed for him, or is his term cut short?
Source pages p. 377

Commentary
This passage is an introductory question for the chapter on lifetimes (الآجال). The author poses a classic theological problem: when a person is killed, does he die at the exact moment that God had decreed for his natural death, or does the killing interrupt and shorten that term? The question presupposes that every person has a fixed appointed term (أجل) from God. The two alternatives reflect different understandings of divine decree and human action: one view holds that the term remains unchanged regardless of cause of death, while the other suggests that violence can cut the term short. This question sets up the discussion that follows in the chapter.

Key Terms
الآجال
المقتول
الأجل
مقطوع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the question denies predestination.
Correction: The question actually explores how predestination relates to secondary causes like killing.

Checkpoint
The question posed at the beginning of the chapter asks whether the killed person dies:
A) at his natural term or it is shortened
B) by his own choice
C) before his term always
D) after his term

Key Takeaway
The central question of the chapter is whether the killed person dies at his predetermined term or has it cut short, framing the debate on divine decree and human action.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have a fixed term known only to God. Does knowing that your death is written make you more careful with your life, or less? What would change if you truly lived each day as if it could be your last?
?
When you hear of someone being killed, do you feel a sense of injustice or do you accept it as part of God's decree? How does your heart respond to the tension between human responsibility and divine predestination?
?
If you were to die tonight, would you die at your 'appointed term' or would you feel that something was cut short? What does that feeling reveal about your trust in God's wisdom and timing?

Refuting the Mu'tazila: The Slain Dies at His Appointed Term
Baqillani refutes the Mu'tazila on the slain's term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Mu'tazila claim that the slain dies before his term is false, and how the Asha'ira affirm that every person dies exactly at the term written by Allah.

Core Idea
Allah's decree determines the term; no act of another can cut it short.

The Mu'tazila argued that a person killed unjustly dies before his appointed time, implying that human action can override divine decree. In this passage, Imam Baqillani refutes this by affirming that the slain person dies at his own term set by Allah, using a clear analogy to illustrate that what Allah does not preserve was never decreed as the term.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysing, then the translation. Notice how Baqillani frames the Mu'tazila position and then refutes it.
The passage begins with 'وقد قال كثير من المعتزلة'.
2
Understand the Mu'tazila claim
Identify the exact claim: the slain died before his term; if not killed, he would have lived. This is the error being refuted.
3
Analyse the refutation
Baqillani says the slain dies at his term, not because of the killer. God could have extended his life but did not, so the time before death was not his term. The analogy of the unmarried woman clarifies this.
The word 'أنفه' might be misread; the translation treats it as a conditional.
4
Reflect on the analogy
The woman who could have been married but wasn't is not a wife. Similarly, the extra years the slain could have lived were not his term because Allah did not decree them.
This shows that possibility does not imply actuality in divine decree.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال كثير من المعتزلة إلا من شد منهم، إن المقتول مات بغير أجله الذي ضرب له، وإنه لو لم يُقتل لحيي. وهذا غلط عندنا، لأن المقتول لم يمت من أجل قتل غيره له، بل [أنفه؟] أو قتل فإنما مات بأجله الذي جعله الله عز وجل أجلاً لعمره. والله قادر على إبقائه والزيادة في عمره لكنه إذا لم يبقه إلى مدة لم تكن المدة التي لم يبق إليها أجلاً له. كما أن المرأة التي لم يتزوجها قبل موته لم تكن امرأة له وإن أمكن أن يتزوجها لو لم يمت. وزعم بعض القدرية أن المقتول مقطوع عليه أجله. فجعلوا العباد قادرين على أن ينقضوا مما أجله الله عز وجل ووقته. ولو جاز ذلك لجاز أن يزيدوا في أجل من قضى الله له أجلاً محدوداً. وإذا لم يقدروا على الزيادة في أجل آخر لم يقدروا على النقصان منه. فأما قول نوح عليه السلام (ويؤخركم إلى أجل مسمى) فإنه لم يقل ويؤخركم إلى أجل لكم. ونحن لا ننكر إمكان البقاء إن لو لم يمت المقتول ولكنا قلنا إن المدة التي قتل قبلها لم تكن أجلاً له. احتجوا بقوله تعالى : (وما يعمر من معمر ولا ينقص من عمره). وقال أكثر القدرية المقتول ميت وفيه معنيان أحدهما موت من فعل الله عز وجل والثاني قتل هو من فعل القاتل. وقال أصحابنا القتل غير الموت ولكن المقتول ميت والموت قائم به والقتل يقوم بالقاتل.
And many of the Mu'tazila, except the extreme among them, have said that the slain person died at other than his term that was appointed for him, and that if he had not been killed he would have lived. And this is an error according to us, because the slain person did not die because of another's killing him, but [rather?] if he is killed, he dies at his term which Allah Mighty and Majestic made the term of his life. And Allah is able to preserve him and increase his life, but when He does not preserve him until a period, that period to which He did not preserve him is not a term for him. Just as a woman whom a man did not marry before his death is not his wife, even though he could have married her if he had not died. And some of the Qadariyya claimed that the slain person's term is cut off. So they made servants able to break what Allah Mighty and Majestic has appointed and timed. And if that were permissible, it would be permissible for them to increase the term of one for whom Allah decreed a fixed term. And since they are not able to increase another's term, they are not able to decrease it. As for the saying of Noah, peace be upon him, (And He will postpone you to a named term), he did not say 'postpone you to your term.' And we do not deny the possibility of survival if the slain person had not died, but we say that the period before which he was killed was not a term for him. They argued with His saying, Most High: (And no one is given long life nor is his life shortened). And most of the Qadariyya said: The slain person is dead, and it contains two meanings: one is death from the act of Allah Mighty and Majestic, and the second is killing which is the act of the killer. And our companions (Asha'ira) said: Killing is not death, but the slain person is dead, and death inheres in him, and killing inheres in the killer.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two deviant sects: the Mu'tazila (except the extreme) who claim the slain dies before his appointed term, and the Qadariyya who say the term is cut off by human action. The author first refutes the Mu'tazila: the slain does not die because of the killer's act; rather, he dies at his own term set by God. God could have preserved him, but did not; so the time before which he died was not his term. An analogy: a woman a man never marries is not his wife, even though he could have married her. Then the Qadariyya are refuted: if humans could cut off a term, they could also extend it—which they cannot. Then the objection from Noah's verse is answered: Noah said 'postpone you to a named term' (from God), not 'to your own term'; so the term is fixed. The response to the verse 'nor is his life shortened' is implicit: the shortening is from God, not from the killer. Finally, the Asha'ira position is stated: killing is not death; death is an act of God that occurs at the fixed term, while killing is an act of the killer. This preserves both divine decree and human accountability.

Key Terms
المعتزلة
القتل
الموت
الأجل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The slain dies before his appointed term because of the killer's act.
Correction: The slain dies exactly at his term; the killer's act is only the means, and Allah could have extended the life but did not.

Checkpoint
What is the core of the Mu'tazila claim that Baqillani refutes?
A) That the slain was not killed by anyone.
B) That the slain dies before his term and would have lived if not killed.
C) That the killer dies instead of the slain.
D) That the term is the same for everyone.

Key Takeaway
Every person dies exactly at the term Allah has written for him; no human act can change that appointed time.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every moment of your life—including the moment of your death—is exactly as Allah has written? If you really believed that, would you be less anxious about the future?
?
When you see someone die unexpectedly, perhaps young or by violence, does a part of you question Allah's wisdom? This lesson says their term was exactly as He decreed. How can you train your heart to accept that without reservation?
?
Are you living as if you can control how long you have? What would change in your priorities if you acted with the certain knowledge that your death is at the very moment Allah appointed and not a second before or after?
