The Qadariyya Error and the Asha'ira Position on Killing and Death
Baqillani refutes Qadariyya, answers objections, and states Asha'ira position.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the Qadariyya claim that the term can be cut off by human action is false, how the objection from Noah's verse is answered, and how the Asha'ira distinguish between killing (human act) and death (divine act).

Core Idea
Allah alone sets the term; human acts do not alter it. Killing is not death.

Having refuted the Mu'tazila, Baqillani turns to the Qadariyya who claim the slain's term is 'cut off' by the killer. He argues that if humans could cut off a term, they could also extend it—which they cannot. He then answers objections from Noah's verse and from the Quranic verse about shortening of life, and finally presents the Asha'ira position: killing is a human act, death is a divine act that occurs at the fixed term.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation. Note the progression: refutation of Qadariyya, answer to objections, and the final doctrinal statement.
The passage includes a verse from Surah Noah and Surah Fatir.
2
Identify the Qadariyya claim
They say the term is 'cut off' by the killer, implying humans can override Allah's decree.
3
Analyse the refutation
Baqillani uses a parallelism: if you could decrease the term, you could also increase it. Since you cannot increase, you cannot decrease. This shows the absurdity.
4
Understand the answers to objections
From Noah's verse: 'postpone you to a named term' means from Allah, not your own term. From the Quran: 'nor is his life shortened' refers to divine decree, not human action.
The original Quranic verse is from Surah Fatir 35:11.
5
Grasp the Asha'ira distinction
Killing is an act of the killer; death is an act of Allah that inheres in the slain. They are distinct. This preserves both divine decree and human accountability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد قال كثير من المعتزلة إلا من شد منهم، إن المقتول مات بغير أجله الذي ضرب له، وإنه لو لم يُقتل لحيي. وهذا غلط عندنا، لأن المقتول لم يمت من أجل قتل غيره له، بل [أنفه؟] أو قتل فإنما مات بأجله الذي جعله الله عز وجل أجلاً لعمره. والله قادر على إبقائه والزيادة في عمره لكنه إذا لم يبقه إلى مدة لم تكن المدة التي لم يبق إليها أجلاً له. كما أن المرأة التي لم يتزوجها قبل موته لم تكن امرأة له وإن أمكن أن يتزوجها لو لم يمت. وزعم بعض القدرية أن المقتول مقطوع عليه أجله. فجعلوا العباد قادرين على أن ينقضوا مما أجله الله عز وجل ووقته. ولو جاز ذلك لجاز أن يزيدوا في أجل من قضى الله له أجلاً محدوداً. وإذا لم يقدروا على الزيادة في أجل آخر لم يقدروا على النقصان منه. فأما قول نوح عليه السلام (ويؤخركم إلى أجل مسمى) فإنه لم يقل ويؤخركم إلى أجل لكم. ونحن لا ننكر إمكان البقاء إن لو لم يمت المقتول ولكنا قلنا إن المدة التي قتل قبلها لم تكن أجلاً له. احتجوا بقوله تعالى : (وما يعمر من معمر ولا ينقص من عمره). وقال أكثر القدرية المقتول ميت وفيه معنيان أحدهما موت من فعل الله عز وجل والثاني قتل هو من فعل القاتل. وقال أصحابنا القتل غير الموت ولكن المقتول ميت والموت قائم به والقتل يقوم بالقاتل.
And many of the Mu'tazila, except the extreme among them, have said that the slain person died at other than his term that was appointed for him, and that if he had not been killed he would have lived. And this is an error according to us, because the slain person did not die because of another's killing him, but [rather?] if he is killed, he dies at his term which Allah Mighty and Majestic made the term of his life. And Allah is able to preserve him and increase his life, but when He does not preserve him until a period, that period to which He did not preserve him is not a term for him. Just as a woman whom a man did not marry before his death is not his wife, even though he could have married her if he had not died. And some of the Qadariyya claimed that the slain person's term is cut off. So they made servants able to break what Allah Mighty and Majestic has appointed and timed. And if that were permissible, it would be permissible for them to increase the term of one for whom Allah decreed a fixed term. And since they are not able to increase another's term, they are not able to decrease it. As for the saying of Noah, peace be upon him, (And He will postpone you to a named term), he did not say 'postpone you to your term.' And we do not deny the possibility of survival if the slain person had not died, but we say that the period before which he was killed was not a term for him. They argued with His saying, Most High: (And no one is given long life nor is his life shortened). And most of the Qadariyya said: The slain person is dead, and it contains two meanings: one is death from the act of Allah Mighty and Majestic, and the second is killing which is the act of the killer. And our companions (Asha'ira) said: Killing is not death, but the slain person is dead, and death inheres in him, and killing inheres in the killer.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of two deviant sects: the Mu'tazila (except the extreme) who claim the slain dies before his appointed term, and the Qadariyya who say the term is cut off by human action. The author first refutes the Mu'tazila: the slain does not die because of the killer's act; rather, he dies at his own term set by God. God could have preserved him, but did not; so the time before which he died was not his term. An analogy: a woman a man never marries is not his wife, even though he could have married her. Then the Qadariyya are refuted: if humans could cut off a term, they could also extend it—which they cannot. Then the objection from Noah's verse is answered: Noah said 'postpone you to a named term' (from God), not 'to your own term'; so the term is fixed. The response to the verse 'nor is his life shortened' is implicit: the shortening is from God, not from the killer. Finally, the Asha'ira position is stated: killing is not death; death is an act of God that occurs at the fixed term, while killing is an act of the killer. This preserves both divine decree and human accountability.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Humans can change the appointed term of death by killing or other actions.
Correction: The term is fixed by Allah alone; human actions do not alter it. Killing and death are distinct—death occurs at the term, while killing is a separate human act.

Checkpoint
How does Baqillani refute the Qadariyya claim that the term can be cut off?
A) By citing a verse from the Quran.
B) By arguing that if one can decrease, one can also increase—which is impossible.
C) By stating that the killer is not responsible.
D) By denying that the slain dies.

Key Takeaway
Killing is a human act, death is a divine act; the term of life is fixed by Allah and cannot be altered by any creature.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

If you truly internalized that no killer can shorten your life by a single moment, would you live differently today? What fear would you release, and what courage would you take?
?
The Qadariyya error was to give humans power over death. Do you still act as if your own efforts—your health choices, your safety precautions—ultimately control your lifespan? How does this lesson shift your trust from yourself to Allah?
?
When you commit a sin that harms another, do you truly accept that the outcome (e.g., their suffering) is also from Allah, while you bear full responsibility for your act? Are you willing to repent without making excuses, knowing that your action is yours alone and the consequence is from Allah?

Refutation: The Murdered Dies by His Term
Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya claim about murder and term.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument against the Qadariyya claim that the murderer cuts short the victim's term, and why the claim is internally inconsistent.

Core Idea
The murderer does not cause death; Allah's decree determines the term.

In this passage, Baqillani directly refutes a core Qadariyya claim: that the murder victim dies before his appointed term. He argues that the victim dies exactly by his term, and that the idea of humans being able to cut short what Allah decreed leads to an absurd consequence. Let's follow his reasoning step by step.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice that Baqillani uses a very direct refutational style here.
2
Identify the main claim
What is the claim Baqillani is refuting? What does he assert instead about the murdered person's death?
The key phrase: 'لم يمت من أجل قتل غيره له'.
3
Understand the analogy
Baqillani gives an analogy of a woman not married before a man's death. Reflect on how this illustrates his point about the term not being changed.
4
Grasp the reductio ad absurdum
Baqillani argues that if humans could cut short a term, they could also extend it. Since they cannot extend, they cannot cut short. This is a logical refutation.
This is the core of the argument against the Qadariyya.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وهذا غلط عندنا، لأن المقتول لم يمت من أجل قتل غيره له، بل أنفه أو قتل فإنما مات بأجله الذي جعله الله عزّ وجلّ أجلاً لعمره والله قادر على إبقائه والزيادة في عمره لكنه إذا لم يبقه إلى مدة لم يكن المدة التي لم يبق إليها أجلاً له. كما أن المرأة التي لم يتزوجها قبل موته لم تكن امرأة له وإن أمكن أن يتزوجها لو لم يمت. وزعم بعض القدرية أن المقتول مقطوع عليه أجله. فجعلوا العباد قادرين على أن ينقضوا مما أجله الله عزّ وجلّ ووقته. ولو جاز ذلك لجاز أن يزيدوا في أجل من قضى الله له أجلاً محدوداً. وإذا لم يقدروا على الزيادة في أجل آخر لم يقدروا على النقصان منه.
And this is a mistake in our view, because the murdered person did not die due to the killing by another, but rather he died by his term which Allah, Mighty and Majestic, made as the term for his life. And Allah is able to preserve him and increase his lifespan, but if He did not preserve him up to a certain time, then that time which He did not preserve him to was not his term. Just as a woman whom a man did not marry before his death was not his wife, even though he could have married her if he had not died. And some of the Qadariyya claimed that the murdered person's term is cut off. Thus they made the servants able to annul what Allah, Mighty and Majestic, has decreed and timed. And if that were permissible, it would be permissible for them to increase the term of one for whom Allah has decreed a fixed term. And since they are not able to increase another's term, they are not able to decrease it.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila claim. The author states that the murdered person does not die because of the killer's action; rather, he dies by his own term, which Allah decreed. Allah could have preserved him longer but did not, so the time he died is his term. An analogy is given: a woman not married before death is not his wife, even though possible. Then the author addresses the Qadariyya who say the murdered person's term is cut off. This implies humans can annul Allah's decree. The author argues by parity: if they could cut short a term, they could also extend it, which is absurd. Thus the original claim is invalid.

Correction: According to Baqillani, the victim dies exactly by his term set by Allah; the killer is merely an instrument. The term is not shortened by human action.

Distinguishing Killing and Death: Baqillani's Response to the Qadariyya
Baqillani interprets Noah's verse and Quran on lifespan, rebutting Qadariyya.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani refutes the Qadariyya claim that human killing can shorten a divinely fixed lifespan, by distinguishing between the act of killing and the act of death.

Core Idea
Killing and death are two distinct accidents; one does not replace the other.

In this passage, Imam al-Baqillani tackles a key Qadari argument: that if a person is killed, his lifespan is cut short, suggesting that humans can alter divine decree. He responds by carefully analyzing two Quranic verses and drawing a sharp distinction between killing (an act of the killer) and death (an act of Allah). This distinction safeguards the doctrine that all lifespans are fixed by Allah alone.

Guided Path
1
Start with Noah's verse
Read Baqillani's clarification of the phrase 'an appointed term' in Noah's verse. Note that the term is fixed by Allah, not the individual.
Baqillani emphasizes that the 'postponement' is to a term already defined by Allah.
2
Examine the Quranic verse on lifespan
Now read how he interprets 'No one to whom a life is granted lives long nor is his life shortened.' He argues this refers to the full, decreed lifespan, not a reduction by killing.
The Qadariyya used this verse to claim lifespan can be shortened.
3
Understand the distinction between killing and death
Baqillani explains that the murdered person is dead, but death inheres in him (from Allah) while killing inheres in the killer. They are two different accidents.
This is the core of his rebuttal.
4
Reject the hypothetical 'if not killed'
Finally, he argues that we cannot say the victim would have lived because killing is not contrary to life; death is. The time of death remains as decreed.
Some Qadariyya even conceded this point.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأما قول نوح عليه السلام ويؤخركم إلى أجل مسمى فإنه لم يقل ويؤخركم إلى أجل لكم. ونحن لا ننكر إمكان البقاء إن لو لم يمت المقتول ولكنا قلنا إن المدة التي قتل قبلها لم تكن أجلاً له. احتجوا بقوله تعالى : وما يعمر من معمر ولا ينقص من عمره. وقال أكثر القدرية المقتول ميت وفيه معنيان أحدهما موت من فعل الله عزّ وجلّ والثاني قتل هو من فعل القاتل. وقال أصحابنا القتل غير الموت ولكن المقتول ميت والموت قائم به والقتل يقوم بالقاتل. من أجل ما فعله الله سبحانه من الموت الذي وُجد به. وليس يجوز أن يقال فيما لم يمت الإنسان من أجله لو لم يكن لحيي. لأن القتل ليس بضدّ للحياة ولا بدل منها، فيقال له إنه لو لم يكن لحيي المقتول. ولأن في ذلك دفع ما تلوناه من التنزيل. وقد قال قوم منهم يجوز أن يحيا لو لم يُقتل، ويجوز أن لا يحيا وأن يكون ذلك الوقت وقت موته.
As for the saying of Noah, peace be upon him: 'And He will postpone you to an appointed term' – he did not say 'to a term for you'. And we do not deny the possibility of survival if the murdered person had not been killed, but we say that the period before which he was killed was not his term. They argued with His saying, Exalted: 'No one to whom a life is granted lives long nor is his life shortened.' And the majority of the Qadariyya said: The murdered person is dead, and in him are two meanings: one is death, which is an act of Allah, and the other is killing, which is an act of the killer. And our companions said: Killing is not death, but the murdered person is dead, and death inheres in him, and killing inheres in the killer. Because of what Allah, Most High, has done of death which came to be through it. And it is not permissible to say regarding something from which the person did not die that if it had not been, he would have lived. Because killing is not contrary to life nor a substitute for it, so that one could say to him: 'If it had not been, the murdered person would have lived.' And because in that is a rejection of what we have recited from the revelation. And some of them said: It is possible that he would have lived if he had not been killed, and it is possible that he would not have lived and that that time was his time of death.
Source pages p. 378

Commentary
This passage addresses two objections. First, Noah's verse: 'He will postpone you to an appointed term' – the Qadariyya might think this implies a term that can be moved. Baqillani clarifies that the term is defined by Allah, not the person. The author then repeats his position: survival after murder is possible, but the time killed was not his term. Second, the Qadariyya cite Quran 35:11 to argue that lifespan can be reduced. The author interprets the verse as referring to a complete lifespan, not reduction by murder. Then a distinction is made: the Mu'tazila say the murdered person has death from Allah and killing from the killer; the Ash'aris say killing is an accident in the killer, while death is an accident in the victim, and the two are distinct. The passage concludes by rejecting the hypothetical 'if he had not been killed, he would have lived' because killing is not a contrary to life that can replace it. Some Mu'tazila conceded that it is not necessary that he would have lived; the time could still be his death time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That human killing can shorten a divinely fixed lifespan, because the Quran says 'nor is his life shortened' implies reduction by external causes.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the verse refers to the complete, decreed lifespan; apparent reduction is not actual reduction. The time of death is fixed by Allah, and killing does not change it.

Key Takeaway

The Impossibility of Extending Lifespan Beyond Divine Decree
Baqillani argues against extending lifespan beyond divine decree.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why Baqillani holds that a person's lifespan cannot be extended beyond the time God decrees for their death, even if God is capable of extending it.

Core Idea
Divine knowledge determines actual lifespan, not mere possibility.

Baqillani confronts a difficult question: if God is all-powerful, could He extend a person's life beyond the moment of death? The answer requires a precise understanding of divine decree. In this passage, he distinguishes between what is possible in God's power and what is actualized by His eternal knowledge. Read on to see how he uses analogy to clarify this.

Guided Path
1
Read the source passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the full translation. Let the argument's flow come through before dissecting it.
Pay attention to the opening statement about death being from God.
2
Identify the core claim
Find where Baqillani states that a person's lifespan is their actual time of death. Notice how he rejects the idea that a slain person would have lived if not killed.
Killing is not the opposite of life; it's an act that terminates it.
3
Examine the analogies
Consider the analogies of Hell/Paradise and the potential wife. How do they support the principle that actuality depends on divine knowledge, not possibility?
These analogies illustrate that what is not decreed cannot be considered part of one's lifespan.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
من أجل ما فعله الله سبحانه من الموت الذي وجد به . وليس يجوز أن يقال فيما لم يمت الإنسان من أجله لو لم يكن لحيي. لأن القتل ليس بضدّ للحياة ولا بدل منها ، فيقال له : «إنه لو لم يكن لحيي المقتول». ولأن في ذلك دفع ما تلوناه من التنزيل . وقد قال قوم منهم : يجوز أن يحيا لو لم يُقتل، ويجوز أن لا يحيا وأن يكون ذلك الوقت وقت موته . فإن قال قائل : فهل كان جائزاً في قدرة الله تعالى أن يُبقي من أماته ابن عشرين سنة إلى ثلاثين سنة أو ما هو أكثر منها ؟ . قيل له : أجل، لو بقاه لبقي. وإن كان لا يفعل ذلك، كان المعلوم حاله أنه يُميته ابن عشرين سنة ، ولن يجوز ترك فعل ما في المعلوم أنه يفعل، وإن كان مقدوراً تركه على أنه لو ترك لكان السابق في المعلوم أنه يترك . فإن قال قائل : فما أنكرتم أن يكون أجله ثلاثين سنة ، لأنه لولم يمته ، لبقي إلى ذلك الوقت؟ . قيل له : لا يجب ذلك، لأن أجل الإنسان وقت موته على ما بينا. وليس أن يكون ما لم يبق إليه، مما كان يصح في العقل أن تمتد حياته إليه أجلاً له، إن كان المعلوم من حاله أنه يُخترم دونه. كما لا يجوز أن تكون جهنّم دار الأنبياء والصالحين وسائر المؤمنين، لأنه جائز في العقل أن يدخلوها لو كفروا، وأن تكون الجنّة دار الفراعنة والكفرة على أنهم لو آمنوا لسكنوها . وكما لا يجب أن تكون المرأة التي يعلم الله أن الإنسان لو بقي لتزوّج بها زوجةً له على معنى أنه لو بقي وتزوجها لكانت زوجة له فكذلك لا يجوز أن يكون ما لم يَبْقَ إليه من الأوقات أجلاً له لأنه لو لم يمت لصح أن يبقى إليه .
Because of what God did—the death that occurred by it. And it is not permissible to say regarding that for which a person did not die that if he had not been [killed] he would have lived. For killing is not opposite to life nor a substitute for it, so it is said to him: 'He would not have lived, the slain man.' And because that would refute what we have recited from the revelation. And some of them said: It is possible that he would live if not killed, and possible that he would not live and that time would be his time of death. If someone says: Was it possible in God's power to keep alive one whom He caused to die at twenty years until thirty years or more? It is said to him: Yes, if He kept him he would remain. But if He does not do that, then the known state of affairs is that He causes him to die at twenty years, and it is not permissible to omit doing what is known that He does, even if it is possible to omit it, such that if He omitted it, the prior [knowledge] would have been that He omits. If someone says: Why do you deny that his lifespan could be thirty years, because if He had not caused him to die, he would have remained until that time? It is said to him: That is not necessary, because a person's lifespan is his time of death as we have explained. And it is not [valid] that a time to which he did not reach—which it was intellectually possible for his life to extend to—be his lifespan, if the known state of affairs concerning him is that he is cut off before it. Just as it is not permissible for Hell to be the abode of prophets, righteous, and all believers, because it is intellectually possible that they would enter it if they disbelieved, and for Paradise to be the abode of Pharaohs and disbelievers given that if they believed they would inhabit it. And just as it is not necessary that a woman whom God knows that if a man remained he would marry be his wife in the sense that if he remained and married her she would be his wife, so too it is not permissible for a time to which he did not reach to be his lifespan, because if he had not died, it would be valid for him to remain until it.
Source pages p. 379

Commentary
This passage is a theological argument about the relationship between divine decree and lifespan. The author begins by stating that death occurs by God's action, and it is invalid to claim that a person who was killed would have lived if not killed, because killing is not the opposite of life nor a substitute—it is an act that terminates life. The author then reports an opposing view: some say the slain person could live or die at that time. The author then presents an objection: If God could keep a person alive longer, why deny that his actual lifespan might be longer? The answer is that God's prior knowledge determines the actual death time; even if He could extend life, His knowledge that He will cause death at a specific time renders that time the actual lifespan, and it is not necessary that a possible future time be considered his lifespan if divine knowledge precludes it. The author uses analogies: Hell is not the actual abode of believers even though it is possible if they disbelieved; a potential wife is not an actual wife if the marriage never occurs. Thus, a time not reached due to divinely decreed death cannot be considered the lifespan.

Key Terms
أجل
الموت
القتل
المعلوم

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if God can extend life, then the actual lifespan must be the maximum possible duration.
Correction: Baqillani argues that divine knowledge determines the actual time of death; mere possibility does not override divine decree.

Checkpoint
Why does Baqillani reject the idea that a slain person's lifespan could have been longer if not killed?
A) Because killing is not opposite to life
B) Because God's knowledge determines the actual time of death
C) Because the Quran says so
D) Because it is intellectually impossible

Key Takeaway
A person's actual lifespan is determined by God's eternal knowledge, not by what is merely possible.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your lifespan is exactly what Allah knows and decrees, then every breath you take is a gift. Are you living with the awareness that each moment is a divine trust, not a guarantee? What would change today if you truly internalized that your death is already written?
?
Do you ever worry about the future—your health, safety, or longevity—as if it were uncertain? This lesson teaches that what is possible is not what is actual; only Allah's knowledge determines reality. Will you surrender that anxiety to Him and trust His decree completely?
?
The analogies of Hell not being for prophets and Paradise not for Pharaohs show that possibilities do not alter actual outcomes in Allah's decree. Is there a 'what if' in your life—a path you think you could have taken—that you still cling to? Can you let go of that imagined reality and submit to what Allah actually wrote for you?

God's Guidance and Misguidance: Affirmation and Scriptural Proof
Baqillani affirms God guides believers and misguides disbelievers, citing Quranic verses.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Baqillani uses Quranic verses to affirm that God is the sole creator of faith and misguidance, and how to distinguish between guidance as creation versus invitation.

Core Idea
God alone creates faith and misguidance; the Quran proves it.

In this passage, Baqillani responds to a key question about divine guidance and misguidance. He affirms that God actively guides believers and misguides disbelievers, supporting this with several Quranic verses. He then clarifies the precise meaning of 'guidance' in these contexts, distinguishing it from other uses in the Quran. This lesson will walk through his argument and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Understand the question
The passage begins with a hypothetical question: Do you say God guides believers and misguides disbelievers? Note that this sets up the orthodox Sunni position.
2
Read the Quranic proofs
Baqillani cites four verses that explicitly attribute guidance and misguidance to God. Read them carefully and notice how each verse ends with God's will.
These verses are from Surah Yunus, Al-Qasas, Al-An'am, and Al-A'raf.
3
Grasp the interpretation
Baqillani insists that 'guidance' in these verses means the creation of faith, not just invitation. Reflect on why this interpretation is crucial for the Sunni doctrine of qadar.
4
Distinguish other meanings
Baqillani acknowledges that 'guidance' can also mean invitation or showing the way to Paradise, but clarifies that these are different from the verses he cited. This prevents misunderstanding.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الهدى والإضلال. فإن قال قائل : فهل تقولون إن الله يهدي المؤمنين ويُضلّ الكافرين؟ . قيل له : أجل . اعلم، وفقك الله تعالى لمرضاته أن كتاب الله العزيز اشتمل على أي دالة على تفرد الرب تعالى بهداية الخلق وإضلالهم. وهي نصوص لإبطال مذاهب مخالفي أهل الحق منها قوله : ﴿ والله يدعو إلى دار السلام ويهدي من يشاء إلى صراط مستقيم ﴾ وقوله تعالى : ﴿ إنك لا تهدي من أحببت ولكن الله يهدي من يشاء ﴾ وقوله تعالى : ﴿ فمن يرد الله أن يهديه يشرح صدره للإسلام ومن يرد أن يضله يجعل صدره ضيقاً حرجاً ﴾ وقال عزّ وجلّ : ﴿ من يهد الله فهو المهتدي ومن يضلل فأولئك هم الخاسرون ﴾ واعلم أن الهدى في هذه الآي لا يتجه حمله إلا على خلق الإيمان، وكذلك لا يتجه حمل الإضلال على غير خلق الضلال ولسنا ننكر ورود الهداية في كتاب الله عزّ وجلّ على غير المعنى الذي رمناه. فقد يرد والمراد به الدعوة ؛ قال الله تعالى : ﴿ إنك لتهدي إلى صراط مستقيم ﴾ معناه إنك لتدعو وقد ترد الهداية ويراد بها إرشاد المؤمنين إلى مسالك الجنان والطرق المفضية إليها يوم القيامة، قال الله تعالى: ﴿ فلن يضل أعمالهم سيهديهم ويصلح بالهم ﴾ .
Chapter on Guidance and Misguidance. If someone says: Do you say that God guides the believers and misguides the disbelievers? It is said to him: Yes. Know—may God guide you to His pleasure—that the Book of God, the Mighty, contains signs indicating the uniqueness of the Lord in guiding creation and leading them astray. They are texts to invalidate the doctrines of those who oppose the people of truth. Among them is His saying: 'And God invites to the abode of peace and guides whom He wills to a straight path.' And His saying: 'Indeed, you do not guide whom you love, but God guides whom He wills.' And His saying: 'Whoever God wants to guide, He expands his breast for Islam; and whoever He wants to lead astray, He makes his breast tight and constricted.' And He said: 'Whoever God guides is the guided one; and whoever He leads astray, those are the losers.' Know that 'guidance' in these verses cannot be interpreted except as the creation of faith, and likewise 'misguidance' cannot be interpreted except as the creation of misguidance. And we do not deny that 'guidance' appears in the Book of God in other senses. It may appear meaning invitation; God said: 'Indeed, you guide to a straight path' meaning you invite. And guidance may appear meaning showing the believers the paths of Paradise and the ways leading to it on the Day of Resurrection; God said: 'He will not let their deeds be lost; He will guide them and set right their condition.'
Source pages p. 380

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal statement and scriptural proof. Baqillani begins by affirming that God guides believers and misguides disbelievers, in response to an implied question. He then urges the reader to recognize that the Quran contains clear signs of God's exclusive control over guidance and misguidance. He cites four Quranic verses that explicitly attribute guidance and misguidance to God alone, arguing that these are proof texts to refute those who deny this (presumably the Mu'tazila). He then clarifies that the term 'guidance' in these verses must be understood as the creation of faith (khalaq al-iman), not merely invitation or showing the way. Similarly, 'misguidance' means the creation of misguidance (khalaq al-dalal). He acknowledges that the word 'guidance' can have other meanings in the Quran, such as invitation (da'wa) or leading to Paradise, but insists that in the verses cited it refers to the divine act of creating faith. This guards against the Mu'tazili view that guidance is only God's showing the way and that humans create their own faith.

ضلال
خلق الإيمان

Misconception: Some think 'guidance' in the Quran always means showing the way or inviting to Islam, and that humans create their own faith.
Correction: Baqillani shows that in these verses 'guidance' means the creation of faith (khalaq al-iman) by God, and 'misguidance' means the creation of disbelief. This affirms that God is the sole creator of both faith and disbelief.

Key Takeaway
God alone creates faith and misguidance in the hearts, as proven by the Quran, and this is the orthodox Sunni position on qadar.

The Meaning of Divine Misguidance for Disbelievers
Baqillani explains that Allah misguides disbelievers by creating their misguidance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Allah's misguidance of disbelievers means He creates their misguidance, and that the term 'guidance' (hidayah) can sometimes mean calling or leading rather than creating faith.

Core Idea
Allah misguides disbelievers by creating their misguidance as an act of justice.

In this passage, Imam Baqillani responds to a question about the meaning of Allah's misguidance of the disbelievers. He clarifies that idlal is a creative act, not merely a label. By interpreting key Quranic verses, he shows that while Allah creates misguidance in the disbelievers, His guidance of the believers is also from Him, and the term 'guidance' can sometimes mean calling or leading.

Guided Path
1
Read the question and answer
Start by reading the hypothetical question about the meaning of Allah's misguidance of disbelievers and Baqillani's response.
2
Understand the creative misguidance
Notice that Baqillani says Allah misguided them by creating their misguidance, which is described as evil and corrupt.
This establishes that idlal is a creative act.
3
Consider the verse about mujahideen
Baqillani refers to a previous argument about Allah guiding the mujahideen. This shows that hidayah (guidance) can also be creative.
He insists the verse should be interpreted as we mentioned, meaning Allah creates guidance.
4
Examine the verse about guiding to Hell
When Allah says 'Guide them to the path of Hellfire', Baqillani interprets 'guide' (ihdu) as 'lead' (usluku), meaning causing them to enter Hell.
This is a different meaning of hidayah: leading, not creating faith.
5
Analyze the Thamud verse
In the verse 'And as for Thamud, We guided them', Baqillani explains that 'We guided them' means 'We called them' (da'wah), because they preferred blindness over the guidance to which they were called.
Here hidayah means calling to guidance, not creating it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قال : فما معنى إضلاله الكافرين؟ . قيل له : قد أضلّهم بأن يخلق ضلالهم قبيحاً فاسداً وقد مرّ فذكر الله تعالى المجاهدين في سبيله وعنى بهم المهاجرين والأنصار، ثم قال سيهديهم، فينبغي حمل الآية على ما ذكرناه وقال الله تعالى في الكفار فاهدوهم إلى صراط الجحيم معناه اسلكوا بهم إليهم، والمعنى بقوله تعالى: ﴿ وأما ثمود فهديناهم الدعوة، ومعنى الآية أنا دعوناهم فاستحبوا العمى على ما دعوا إليه من الهدى.
So if he said: What is the meaning of His misguidance of the disbelievers? It is said to him: He misguided them by creating their misguidance, evil and corrupt. And it has passed that Allah mentioned the mujahideen in His path, meaning the Muhajireen and Ansar, then He said 'He will guide them' – so the verse should be interpreted according to what we mentioned. And Allah said about the disbelievers: 'Guide them to the path of Hellfire' meaning 'lead them to it'. And the meaning of His statement: 'And as for Thamud, We guided them' – the meaning of the verse is that We called them, but they preferred blindness over the guidance to which they were called.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage explains the meaning of idlal (misguidance) for disbelievers. The author asserts that Allah misguides them by creating their misguidance, which is inherently evil and corrupt. He then references a previous discussion about the verse concerning the mujahideen whom Allah promises to guide, confirming that such guidance is also from Allah. He interprets the verse 'Guide them to the path of Hellfire' as meaning 'lead them' (i.e., cause them to enter it). Regarding the verse about Thamud, 'We guided them' (fahadaynahum), he interprets this as 'We called them' (da'wah), not that Allah created guidance for them, because they rejected it. This shows that idlal always means creating misguidance, while hidayah can sometimes mean calling or leading, depending on context.

Refutation of the Qadariyya on Guidance and Misguidance
Baqillani refutes Qadariyya interpretation of hidayah and idlal

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's linguistic and rational refutation of the Qadariyya who limit divine guidance to mere teaching and misguidance to mere naming or punishment.

Core Idea
Divine guidance and misguidance are creative acts, not mere labels.

The Qadariyya claimed that Allah's guidance is only instruction, and His misguidance is only naming someone misguided or punishing them. Baqillani dismantles this view using both language and reason, showing that their interpretation leads to absurdities. This passage is a masterclass in refuting theological errors through integrated argumentation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Qadariyya position
Read the opening lines to grasp what the Qadariyya claimed about hidayah and idlal.
Notice they limit guidance to irshad, du'a, and bayan, and idlal to naming or punishing.
2
Follow the linguistic argument
Notice how Baqillani uses Arabic verb forms to refute the claim that idlal means naming.
The verb for naming someone misguided is 'dallala' (with tashdid), not 'adalla'.
3
Follow the rational argument
See the absurd consequences if idlal meant naming or punishing.
If naming, then Prophet and disbelievers would be guilty of idlal; if punishing, then judges would be guilty.
4
Appreciate the conclusion
See how the only consistent view is that Allah creates guidance and misguidance directly.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وشذت القدرية فزعمت أن الهداية من الله تعالى على معنى الإرشاد والدعاء وإبانة الحق وليس إليه من هداية القلوب شيء. وزعموا أن الإضلال منه على وجهين: أحدهما أن يقال إنه أضل عبداً أنه سماه ضالاً. والثاني على معنى أنه جازاه على ضلالته وقد أخطأوا في بمعنى تأويلهم من طريق اللغة ومن طريق المعنى، فلأن من سمى غيره ضالاً أو نسبه إلى الضلالة فإنما يقال فيه إنه ضلله بالتشديد ولا يقال أضله . وأما من طريق المعنى فمن جهة أن الإضلال من الله لو كان بمعنى التسمية والحكم لوجب أن يقال إن النبي قد أضل الكفرة لأنـه سماهم ضالين وحكم بضلالتهم ووجب أن يقال إن الكفرة والشياطين قد أضلوا المؤمنين والأنبياء لأنهم قد سموهم ضالين ولو كان الإضلال من الله عزّ وجلّ بمعنى العقاب على الضلالة لكان كل من أقام الحد على الزاني والسارق والقاتل والقاذف وشارب الخمر قد أضلهم، لأنه قد جازاهم على ضلالاتهم وفسقهم. وإذا بطل هذا صح أن الهداية والإضلال من الله تعالى على ما ذهبنا إليه دون ما ذهبت القدرية إليه.
And the Qadariyya deviated and claimed that guidance from Allah means guidance (irshad), calling (du'a), and making clear the truth, and that there is nothing from Him regarding guidance of hearts. And they claimed that misguidance from Him is of two types: one that it is said that He misguided a servant by naming him misguided; and the second in the sense that He punished him for his misguidance. And they erred in the meaning of their interpretation from the linguistic and rational ways. For if someone calls another misguided or attributes misguidance to him, it is said about him that he 'dallala' (with tashdid) not 'adalla'. And as for the rational way, from the aspect that if misguidance from Allah were in the sense of naming and judging, then it would be necessary that the Prophet misguised the disbelievers because he named them misguided and judged their misguidance, and it would be necessary that the disbelievers and devils misguised the believers and prophets because they named them misguided. And if misguidance from Allah were in the sense of punishment for misguidance, then everyone who implements the prescribed punishment on the adulterer, thief, murderer, slanderer, and drunkard would have misguised them, because he punished them for their misguidance and transgression. When this is invalidated, the correct position is that guidance and misguidance are from Allah as we hold, not as the Qadariyya hold.
Source pages p. 381

Commentary
This passage refutes the Qadariyya who reduce hidayah to mere teaching and idlal to naming or punishing. The author argues linguistically: the verb 'adalla' is not used for naming someone misguided; rather 'dallala' (with tashdid) is used. Rationally: if idlal meant naming, then prophets and even disbelievers would also be guilty of idlal, which is absurd. If it meant punishing, then any judge who implements the prescribed punishment (hadd) would be guilty of idlal. Thus, the Qadariyya interpretation is invalid, and the correct view is that Allah creates both guidance and misguidance directly.

Key Terms
القدرية
هداية القلوب
إضلال
ضللة بالتشديد
عقاب

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Qadariyya believe that idlal from Allah is merely naming someone misguided or punishing them.
Correction: Baqillani shows that idlal is a creative act of Allah, not a mere label or penalty, using linguistic and rational proof.

Checkpoint
What linguistic argument does Baqillani give against the Qadariyya claim that idlal means naming someone misguided?
A) The verb 'adalla' is used for naming in Arabic.
B) The verb for naming is 'dallala' (with tashdid), not 'adalla'.
C) The Qadariyya do not know Arabic.
D) Naming is not a form of misguidance.

Key Takeaway
The Qadariyya interpretation of idlal is linguistically and rationally untenable; only the view that Allah creates misguidance is coherent.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite 'Ihdina al-sirat al-mustaqeem' in every rak'ah, do you truly believe Allah must create guidance in your heart, or do you assume He just shows the way? How does the passage strip you of that comforting assumption and force you to beg more earnestly?
?
If you ever feel distant from Allah, do you quickly blame your own actions, or have you considered that He may have willed that distance? How does this passage push you to desperate dua rather than self-congratulation or despair?
?
The Qadariyya tried to protect Allah's justice by denying He creates misguidance. But Baqillani shows that alternative is incoherent. Are you ready to submit to a God whose sovereignty includes creating both light and darkness in hearts, even when it unsettles your sense of fairness?

The Qur’anic Proof for Allah’s Guidance and Misguidance
Baqillani cites Qur’an 14:27 and presents the Qadariyya’s reinterpretation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Qur’anic verse that serves as the primary evidence for attributing both guidance and misguidance to Allah, and you will learn the Qadariyya’s misinterpretation of these terms.

Core Idea
Allah explicitly claims both guidance and misguidance as His actions.

Imam Baqillani begins his refutation by presenting a clear Qur’anic proof: the verse 'And Allah misguides the wrongdoers.' He notes that Allah describes Himself as both guiding and misguiding. Then he introduces the Qadariyya, who reinterpret guidance as mere direction and misguidance as either naming someone misguided or punishing them for their misguidance. Baqillani declares that they have erred both linguistically and logically, which sets the stage for the arguments to come.

Guided Path
1
Read the verse and translation
Read the Qur’anic verse and its translation to see the explicit attribution of misguidance to Allah. Note how it pairs with guidance.
2
Identify the Qadariyya's claims
The Qadariyya claimed that guidance is only irshad (direction) and da'wa (calling), and that Allah does not create guidance in hearts. For misguidance, they said it is either naming someone misguided or punishing them. List these claims.
3
Notice the error
Baqillani states that they erred in language and meaning. This tells us that the refutation will have two parts: linguistic and logical.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: وما الدليل على ما قلتهم؟ قيل لهم: يدل على ذلك قوله تعالى: ويضل الله الظالمين. فأخبر أنه يُضل ويهدي ووصف نفسه بذلك. وشذت القدرية فزعمت أن الهداية من الله تعالى على معنى الإرشاد والدعاء وإبانة الحق وليس إليه من هداية القلوب شيء. وزعموا أن الإضلال منه على وجهين: أحدهما أن يقال إنه أضل عبداً أنه سماه ضالاً. والثاني على معنى أنه جازاه على ضلالته وقد أخطأوا في بمعنى تأويلهم من طريق اللغة ومن طريق المعنى، فلأن من سمى غيره ضالاً أو نسبه إلى الضلالة فإنما يقال فيه إنه ضلله بالتشديد ولا يقال أضله. وأما من طريق المعنى فمن جهة أن الإضلال من الله لو كان بمعنى التسمية والحكم لوجب أن يقال إن النبي قد أضل الكفرة لأنه سماهم ضالين وحكم بضلالتهم ووجب أن يقال إن الكفرة والشياطين قد أضلوا المؤمنين والأنبياء لأنهم قد سموهم ضالين ولو كان الإضلال من الله عز وجل بمعنى العقاب على الضلالة لكان كل من أقام الحد على الزاني والسارق والقاتل والقاذف وشارب الخمر قد أضلهم، لأنه قد جازاهم على ضلالاتهم وفسقهم. وإذا بطل هذا صح أن الهداية والإضلال من الله تعالى على ما ذهبنا إليه دون ما ذهبت القدرية إليه. وزعمت الثنوية أن الهداية من النور والضلال من الظلمة. وزعمت المجوس أن الهداية من الإله والإضلال من الشيطان وقد مضى الكلام عليه في توحيد الصانع.
If they say: And what is the evidence for what you have said? It is said to them: His statement, exalted, indicates that: 'And God misguides the wrongdoers' (wa yuḍillu Allāhu al-ẓālimīn). So He informed that He misguides and guides, and He described Himself with that. And the Qadariyya deviated and claimed that guidance from God Almighty is in the sense of direction (irshād) and calling (duʿā') and clarifying the truth, and that there is nothing to Him of the guidance of hearts. And they claimed that misguidance from Him is in two ways: one that it is said that He has misguided a servant by naming him misguided; and the second in the sense that He has recompensed him for his misguidance. And they have erred in the meaning of their interpretation from the perspective of language and from the perspective of meaning. As for the linguistic perspective, because whoever calls another misguided or attributes misguidance to him, it is said about him that he 'ḍallalahu' (with tashdīd) and it is not said 'aḍallah'. And as for from the perspective of meaning, because if misguidance from God were in the sense of naming and judging, it would be necessary that the Prophet (peace be upon him) has misguided the disbelievers because he named them misguided and judged them to be misguided; and it would be necessary that the disbelievers and devils have misled the believers and the prophets because they have named them misguided. And if misguidance from God, mighty and majestic, were in the sense of punishment for misguidance, then everyone who carries out the prescribed punishment (ḥadd) on the fornicator, thief, murderer, slanderer, and wine-drinker would have misguided them, because he has punished them for their misguidance and sin. When this is invalidated, it is established that guidance and misguidance are from God Almighty according to what we have held, not according to what the Qadariyya have held. And the Dualists (Thānawiyya) claimed that guidance is from light and misguidance from darkness. And the Magians (Majūs) claimed that guidance is from God and misguidance from Satan – and the discussion on that has already passed in the treatise on the Oneness of the Creator (tawḥīd al-Ṣāniʿ).
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage provides scriptural evidence and refutes heretical views on guidance and misguidance. It begins with a proof from the Qur'an: 'And God misguides the wrongdoers' (Ibrahim 14:27), showing that Allah attributes to Himself both guiding and misguiding. Then it refutes the Qadariyya, who claimed that guidance is only direction and calling, not creation of faith, and that misguidance is only naming or punishment. The author argues linguistically: to call someone misguided requires the form 'ḍallala' (with tashdid), not 'aḍalla'. Logically, if misguidance were mere naming, then the Prophet and even disbelievers could also misguide. If it were punishment, then human judges who carry out hadd punishments would also be misguiders. Both consequences are absurd, so the Qadariyya interpretation is invalid. The correct view is that Allah creates guidance and misguidance in the hearts. The passage also mentions the Dualists (Thānawiyya) who attribute guidance to light and misguidance to darkness, and the Magians who attribute misguidance to Satan, but notes that these have already been refuted in the discussion on tawḥīd.

Misconception: Some think that guidance from Allah only means showing the way, not creating faith.
Correction: Baqillani shows that the Qur’anic verse and the arguments to follow prove that Allah creates both guidance and misguidance in the heart, not just outward direction.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what scriptural evidence does Baqillani provide?
A) 'And Allah misguides the wrongdoers'
B) 'Allah guides whom He wills'
C) 'There is no compulsion in religion'
D) 'And whoever Allah guides, none can misguide'

Key Takeaway
The Qur’an explicitly attributes both guidance and misguidance to Allah, and the Qadariyya’s reinterpretation is linguistically and logically flawed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you read that Allah says 'He misguides the wrongdoers,' does your heart tremble at the thought of being among them? In what subtle ways do you try to distance yourself from the label 'wrongdoer' without truly examining your own sins?
?
The Qadariyya reformed the clear words of the Qur'an to avoid a difficult truth. Where in your own life have you reinterpreted Allah's commands or attributes to make them more comfortable, rather than submitting to their full weight?
?
If guidance of the heart truly comes only from Allah—as this verse proves—how often do you beg Him for it with the same desperation you would have if you were physically lost? What needs to change in your du'a today?

Linguistic and Logical Refutation of the Qadariyya
Baqillani presents linguistic and logical refutation, then mentions other sects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic and rational arguments that disprove the Qadariyya’s interpretation of misguidance, and you will see how these arguments establish that Allah creates misguidance in the hearts.

Core Idea
The Arabic language and logical consistency prove that misguidance from Allah is not mere naming or punishment.

In this lesson, Baqillani unpacks his earlier statement that the Qadariyya erred linguistically and rationally. He first explains that if someone is called misguided, the correct Arabic verb is 'ḍallala' (with tashdid), not 'aḍalla' — which is used only for causing misguidance. Then he shows that if misguidance were mere naming, then even the Prophet and disbelievers would be misguiders, which is absurd. Similarly, if misguidance were punishment, then human judges would also misguide. These consequences demolish the Qadariyya position.

Guided Path
1
Understand the linguistic argument
Read the Arabic distinction between ḍallala (to call someone misguided) and aḍalla (to cause misguidance). Note that the Qur’an uses aḍalla, proving it means more than naming.
2
Reflect on the first reductio
If misguidance were naming, then the Prophet would have misguided disbelievers (by naming them misguided), and disbelievers would have misguided believers (by naming them misguided). Is that acceptable? No.
3
Reflect on the second reductio
If misguidance were punishment, then any judge implementing legal penalties would be a misguider. That is clearly false.
4
Conclude the correct view
Baqillani concludes that guidance and misguidance are from Allah in the way the Ahl al-Sunna believe: He creates them in the hearts. Briefly note the mention of Dualists and Magians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: وما الدليل على ما قلتهم؟ قيل لهم: يدل على ذلك قوله تعالى: ويضل الله الظالمين. فأخبر أنه يُضل ويهدي ووصف نفسه بذلك. وشذت القدرية فزعمت أن الهداية من الله تعالى على معنى الإرشاد والدعاء وإبانة الحق وليس إليه من هداية القلوب شيء. وزعموا أن الإضلال منه على وجهين: أحدهما أن يقال إنه أضل عبداً أنه سماه ضالاً. والثاني على معنى أنه جازاه على ضلالته وقد أخطأوا في بمعنى تأويلهم من طريق اللغة ومن طريق المعنى، فلأن من سمى غيره ضالاً أو نسبه إلى الضلالة فإنما يقال فيه إنه ضلله بالتشديد ولا يقال أضله. وأما من طريق المعنى فمن جهة أن الإضلال من الله لو كان بمعنى التسمية والحكم لوجب أن يقال إن النبي قد أضل الكفرة لأنه سماهم ضالين وحكم بضلالتهم ووجب أن يقال إن الكفرة والشياطين قد أضلوا المؤمنين والأنبياء لأنهم قد سموهم ضالين ولو كان الإضلال من الله عز وجل بمعنى العقاب على الضلالة لكان كل من أقام الحد على الزاني والسارق والقاتل والقاذف وشارب الخمر قد أضلهم، لأنه قد جازاهم على ضلالاتهم وفسقهم. وإذا بطل هذا صح أن الهداية والإضلال من الله تعالى على ما ذهبنا إليه دون ما ذهبت القدرية إليه. وزعمت الثنوية أن الهداية من النور والضلال من الظلمة. وزعمت المجوس أن الهداية من الإله والإضلال من الشيطان وقد مضى الكلام عليه في توحيد الصانع.
If they say: And what is the evidence for what you have said? It is said to them: His statement, exalted, indicates that: 'And God misguides the wrongdoers' (wa yuḍillu Allāhu al-ẓālimīn). So He informed that He misguides and guides, and He described Himself with that. And the Qadariyya deviated and claimed that guidance from God Almighty is in the sense of direction (irshād) and calling (duʿā') and clarifying the truth, and that there is nothing to Him of the guidance of hearts. And they claimed that misguidance from Him is in two ways: one that it is said that He has misguided a servant by naming him misguided; and the second in the sense that He has recompensed him for his misguidance. And they have erred in the meaning of their interpretation from the perspective of language and from the perspective of meaning. As for the linguistic perspective, because whoever calls another misguided or attributes misguidance to him, it is said about him that he 'ḍallalahu' (with tashdīd) and it is not said 'aḍallah'. And as for from the perspective of meaning, because if misguidance from God were in the sense of naming and judging, it would be necessary that the Prophet (peace be upon him) has misguided the disbelievers because he named them misguided and judged them to be misguided; and it would be necessary that the disbelievers and devils have misled the believers and the prophets because they have named them misguided. And if misguidance from God, mighty and majestic, were in the sense of punishment for misguidance, then everyone who carries out the prescribed punishment (ḥadd) on the fornicator, thief, murderer, slanderer, and wine-drinker would have misguided them, because he has punished them for their misguidance and sin. When this is invalidated, it is established that guidance and misguidance are from God Almighty according to what we have held, not according to what the Qadariyya have held. And the Dualists (Thānawiyya) claimed that guidance is from light and misguidance from darkness. And the Magians (Majūs) claimed that guidance is from God and misguidance from Satan – and the discussion on that has already passed in the treatise on the Oneness of the Creator (tawḥīd al-Ṣāniʿ).

Refuting the Claim that Guidance is Just a Label
Baqillani refutes the claim that divine guidance and misguidance are mere designation through reductio ad absurdum.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Baqillani's argument that divine guidance and misguidance are real acts, not mere labels, based on Quranic verses and consensus.

Core Idea
Divine guidance is a real gift, not just a label.

This passage tackles a subtle objection: maybe God's 'leading astray' is just a name. Baqillani uses the Qur'an and consensus to show this reduces divine favor to human favor and leads to absurdities. Let's read his refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection and initial proof
Start by reading the opponent's request for evidence and Baqillani's citation of the Qur'anic verse 'And Allah leads the wrongdoers astray.'
The verse shows God describes Himself with actual leading astray.
2
Understand the opponent's counter-argument
The opponent then argues that 'guidance' and 'misguidance' might be mere judicial or nominal designations, like when people label someone astray without causing the condition.
3
Analyze the first reductio: label reduces divine favor
Baqillani argues that if guidance were just a label, God's favor would be no different from one believer labeling another, contradicting the Qur'anic verse that only God confers guidance as a favor.
The verse 'Rather, Allah confers favor upon you that He has guided you' would be invalid if guidance were a mere label.
4
Analyze the second reductio: calling reduces to human level
If guidance were just calling and explaining (da'wa and bayan), then any believer could do that, making God's favor ordinary, which is contrary to consensus.
This also implies Iblis would have led prophets astray by calling them to sin.
5
See the final absurdity and consensus
Baqillani concludes that if guidance were merely designation, Iblis would have led the prophets astray, and the Prophet would have led disbelievers astray, which is rejected by the consensus of the ummah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فإن قالوا: وما الدليل على ما قلتهم؟ . قيل لهم: يدل على ذلك قوله تعالى: ويضل الله الظالمين . فأخبر أنه يُضل ويهدي ووصف نفسه بذلك . فإن قال قائل: ما أنكرتم أن لا يكون معنى الإضلال منه والهداية أكثر من الحكم والتسمية، كما يقول الناس: قد ضلل فلان فلاناً، و«قد عدّله»، وقد سرق فلان فلاناً، لا على معنى أنه جعله ضالا فاسقاً سارقاً وفعل له ما من أجله يكون كذلك والضلال والعدالة ؟ . قيل له: لو كان ذلك على ما قلته، لم يكن الله على المؤمنين في هدايته لهم إلا ما لبعضهم على بعض، لأنَّا قد يسمّي بعضنا بعضاً بالهداية ويخصّ بعضنا بعضاً بهذه التسمية . وكذلك كان يجب أن يكون إضلال بعضنا بعضاً كإضلال الله الظالمين وهذا خلاف ما اتفق عليه المسلمون . لأن الله عزّ وجلّ قد امتن على المؤمنين بهدايته فقال: يمنون عليك أن أسلموا قل لا تمنوا علي إسلامكم بل الله يمن عليكم أن هداكم للإيمان إن كنتم صادقين * فلو كانت هدايته لهم هي الحكم والتسمية، لكانوا قد منّوا على أنفسهم بهذه المنّة، ولكان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم قد من بها عليهم كمنّ الله، إذ قد سماهم بذلك وحكم لهم به وهذا خلاف الإجماع . وكذلك لو كانت هدايته لهم التي من بها عليهم هي دعوته إياهم وبيانه لهم، لكان بعضهم قد منَّ على بعض بهذه المنة. لأنه قد يدعو بعضهم بعضاً ويبين بعضهم لبعض كما يدعو الله وهذا أيضاً خلاف الاتفاق. وعلى أنه لو كانت الهداية والإضلال من الله تعالى بمعنى ما وصفتم، لكان إبليس قد أضل الأنبياء وسائر المؤمنين، إذ كان قد دعاهم إلى الضلال وسمَّاهم ضالين وحكم لهم بذلك؛ ولكان النبي صلى الله عليه وآله وسلم والمؤمنون قد أضلوا الكافرين أجمعين، إذ كانوا قد سموهم كافرين وحكموا لهم بحكم الضالين. وفي إجماع الأمة على خلاف هذا دليل على سقوط ما قلتم .
If they say: And what is the evidence for what you say? It is said to them: That is indicated by His statement, the Most High: 'And Allah leads the wrongdoers astray.' So He informed that He leads astray and guides, and described Himself with that. Then if a speaker says: Why do you deny that the meaning of misguidance and guidance from Him is nothing more than judgment and designation, as people say: 'So-and-so has led so-and-so astray', and 'he has declared him upright', and 'so-and-so has stolen from so-and-so', not meaning that he made him an astray sinner, a thief, and did to him that on account of which he becomes so, and [similarly for] misguidance and uprightness? It is said to him: If that were as you said, then God would not have any more favor on the believers in His guidance than some of them have on others, because we may designate some of us as guided and single out some of us with this designation. And likewise, it would be necessary that the misguidance of some of us by others be like the misguidance of the wrongdoers by God, and this is contrary to what the Muslims have agreed upon. Because God, Almighty and Majestic, has bestowed favor on the believers through His guidance, saying: 'They consider it a favor to you that they have accepted Islam. Say, Do not consider your Islam a favor to me. Rather, Allah confers favor upon you that He has guided you to the faith, if you should be truthful.' So if His guidance to them were the judgment and designation, they would have conferred favor on themselves with this favor, and the Messenger of God, may God bless him and his family and grant them peace, would have conferred favor on them like God's favor, since he designated them as such and judged them accordingly, and this is contrary to consensus. And likewise, if His guidance to them with which He favored them were His calling them and explaining to them, then some of them would have conferred favor on others with this favor, because some of them may call others and explain to others just as God calls, and this too is contrary to agreement. And furthermore, if guidance and misguidance from God Almighty were in the sense you described, then Iblis would have led the prophets and all believers astray, since he called them to misguidance and designated them as astray and judged them as such; and the Prophet, may God bless him and his family and grant them peace, and the believers would have led all the disbelievers astray, since they designated them as disbelievers and judged them with the judgment of the astray. And the consensus of the community contrary to this is evidence of the invalidity of what you say.
Source pages p. 382

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer unit within a larger discussion on divine guidance and misguidance. The opponent first asks for evidence that God actually leads astray and guides, not merely names or judges. Baqillani cites the Qur'anic verse 'And Allah leads the wrongdoers astray' as evidence that God describes Himself with actual leading astray and guiding. The opponent then raises a counter-objection: perhaps 'guidance' and 'misguidance' are simply judicial or nominal designations, like when people say 'so-and-so led him astray' meaning only that they labeled him as astray, not that they caused the condition. Baqillani refutes this with two reductio arguments. First, if guidance were merely a label, then God's favor on believers would be no different from one believer labeling another as guided—a mundane act, not a unique divine favor. The Qur'anic verse about the believers not conferring favor on the Prophet for their Islam, but rather God conferring favor on them, would be incoherent if guidance were just a label, because then they could have conferred that favor on themselves. Second, if guidance were merely invitation and explanation (da'wa and bayan), then any believer could do that, and even Iblis would have 'led the prophets astray' by calling them to sin and labeling them astray, which is absurd by consensus. Similarly, the Prophet and believers would have 'led the disbelievers astray' by calling them and labeling them as astray, which contradicts the Muslim consensus that only God truly leads astray. Thus, the consensus of the ummah proves that the opponent's interpretation is invalid.

Key Takeaway

Repentance Does Not Remove Punishment in This World
Imam Baqillani argues that repentance does not prove reward in the afterlife.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Baqillani's argument that repentance in this world does not guarantee reward in the afterlife, and that worldly punishments are trials rather than proofs of damnation.

Core Idea
Repentance does not erase worldly punishment, so it does not prove afterlife reward.

Imam Baqillani engages with an objection that worldly punishment is a trial, not a punishment. He argues that if repentance guaranteed reward, it would erase punishment in this world, but experience shows repentant sinners are still punished. He then addresses the counterargument that such punishment is a trial, showing that even faithful believers are tried, so the analogy fails.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic text once, then the English translation. Pay attention to the logical flow.
Notice the conditional structure at the beginning.
2
Identify the initial argument
The author posits that if repentance merited reward, it would remove worldly punishment. Find this statement.
3
Identify the objection
The opponents argue that worldly punishment is a trial, not a punishment, so repentance need not remove it. Locate this objection.
4
Analyze the author's response
See how Baqillani turns the objection back on the opponents: the same reasoning applies to believers, so the objection does not disprove his point.
5
Reflect on the Quranic citation
The verse from Surah Al-Ma'idah is cited to support that punishment is for those who consider fornication lawful, not for the repentant.
This shows that punishment in this world does not negate faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم يقال لهم : و لو كان مع التائب المنيب ما يستحق عليه الثواب في الآخرة ، لاستحق به إزالة العقاب والحدود في الدنيا. فلما كان التائب عندنا وعندهم مقطوعاً ومحدوداً مع توبته، بطل أن يكون من أهل التعظيم والثواب في الآخرة . فإن قالوا : إنما لم تُزل التوبة قطع التائب وتعمل في إحباطه لأجل أن قطعه وإقامة الحدود عليه ليس بعقاب وإهانة، وإنما هو محنة من عزّ وجلَّ له . وليس يجب أن تؤثر التوبة في إزالة المحن التي ليست بنكال ولا عقاب . قيل لهم : وكذلك قطع المؤمن الموحد المصدق الله ولرسوله ليس بعقاب ولا نكال وإنما هو امتحان من الله . وإنما المراد بقوله : نكالا الله : إن كانا مستحلين للزنى وممن قد حكم بعقابهما في الآخرة . فلذلك لم يُزِل إيمانُهُ وولايته قطعه وحده
Then it is said to them: If the repentant one who returns (to God) had with him what deserves reward in the afterlife, he would deserve by it the removal of punishment and prescribed penalties in this world. But since the repentant one, according to us and to them, is amputated and subjected to prescribed penalties despite his repentance, it is invalid that he be among the people of honor and reward in the afterlife. So if they say: "Repentance did not remove the amputation of the repentant one and does not nullify (punishment) because his amputation and the execution of prescribed penalties upon him are not punishment and humiliation, but rather a trial from God Almighty, and repentance should not affect the removal of trials that are not a penalty nor punishment." It is said to them: Likewise, the amputation of the believing monotheist who affirms God and His Messenger is not punishment nor penalty, but rather a test from God. And what is meant by His saying "as a penalty from God" (Surah Al-Ma'idah 5:38) is if they are considerers of fornication lawful and among those whose punishment in the afterlife has been decreed. Therefore, his faith and loyalty do not remove his amputation alone.
Source pages p. 417

Commentary
This passage is a dialectical argument with objection and answer. The author begins by presenting a hypothetical: if a repentant sinner deserved reward in the afterlife, he would also deserve removal of punishment in this world. But experience shows that the repentant are still punished (e.g., amputated for theft), so they cannot be assured of reward. An objector then argues that physical punishment in this world is not a punishment but a trial, so repentance need not avert it. The author responds by applying the same reasoning to the believing monotheist: his punishment is also a trial, yet his faith does not exempt him from punishment. The Quranic verse about theft (5:38) is cited to show that the punishment applies unless fornication is considered lawful. Thus, the analogy fails to prove reward.

Key Terms
تائب
ثواب
عقاب
حدود
محنة
نكال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some assume that if someone repents, they will not be punished in this world, implying that worldly punishment shows divine displeasure and loss of afterlife reward.
Correction: Baqillani shows that worldly punishment can be a trial (محنة) that does not negate faith or potential reward; thus, punishment in this world does not prove one is damned in the afterlife.

Checkpoint
What is the main point of the author's argument in this passage?
A) Repentance always removes punishment in this world.
B) Punishment in this world proves one does not deserve reward in the afterlife.
C) Trials and punishments are distinct from rewards.
D) The repentant are never punished.

Key Takeaway
Worldly punishment does not negate the possibility of afterlife reward; repentance does not guarantee immunity from trials in this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sincerely repent but still face the consequences of your sin in this life, do you secretly doubt that your repentance was accepted? What does that reveal about your understanding of God's mercy and justice?
?
If you knew that repentance does not remove worldly trials, would you still repent with the same urgency? What does your answer tell you about the purity of your intention?
?
Think of a time you witnessed or experienced a hardship after repentance. Did you view it as a trial or as an indication of rejection? How does Baqillani's argument challenge you to reinterpret that experience?
